- Understanding, thinking and criticizing Cheerfulism.
- Understanding how to create a frame for thought and create your own philosophy. It does not need to be useful, but it should be created.

Mastery of statistics.

- All students should master an almost university degree level on statistics.
- Being able to explain and interpret statistical results of data and draw logically correct conclusions from them.
- Knowing all basic math required to understand statistics to that level.

Technology usage and understanding.

- Mastery of useful technologies. Currently these are: internet, AI, blockchain, cars, air conditioner…
- Understanding at a high level their internal workings.

Biotechnological technologies can also be included into the understanding section.

Play and rest.

- Learning to enjoy and play alone.
- Learning to enjoy and play with others. The more diverse the others are the better, yet without forcing it.
- Practice at least one art of personal interest, just for the sake of doing it, not to necessarily master it.

Through play and art, emotions handling capabilities should be increased. That is why I did not reference any psychological help techniques on the curriculum. They should naturally emerge in humans that seek for intelligence, explore, think, play, and make art together.

However, a subject for psychological emotional management is not discouraged.

Survival skills.

This subject must be added at some point, yet it is understandable, due to the unlikely usage of their teachings, its delay in the curriculum implementation.

- Learn hunting techniques. No need to practice them, but at least knowing them.
- Learn crops harvesting techniques.
- Learn basic hut building techniques. Using wood, branches, mud, stones...
- Learning to make fire.
- Learning safe exploration techniques.

Learning.

- Full understanding of the engineers’ way of thinking.
- Understanding of different learning techniques and strategies.
- Understanding, at a high level, of the biological reactions that affect human behavior and cognition.
- Having learned something requiring 200 hours of focused effort. This has to be in something you do not like. To cultivate resilience in case life requires you to specialize in unexpected stuff.

Language.

- Mastery speaking in the nation’s language and a common world-wide used language. Like English.
- Mastery of writing on the languages previously mentioned.
- Mastery of reading on the languages mentioned.

All these are the basic curriculum everyone should know and have gone through. This should lead, based on the reasons explained all along, to raising independent and cooperating citizens.

Not following this curriculum will just increase the likelihood of scams on higher levels of education and just trhough life.

Finally and again, how to teach it, with more centralized systems, more decentralized, homework, not homework etc will depend on each nation current situation.

Of crouse, I prefer the ideas mentioned earlier, where decentralized small amounts of population and professionals can pick teachers and create schools easily with trust and responsibility, all leveraged with new technologies and filtering for the qualities of the good teacher explained previously.

Regardless of that, the key principles stated and the basic curriculum are essential. And probably you have noticed, part of them are explained and explored in this book.

Now, if you do not know well enough any of these things on the basic curriculum, what are you waiting for? Let’s start learning them. Even if it is just 1 afternoon every week.

And what about you and a friend? He learns one part, you learn the other, and then you teach each other. If you do so, good luck! If not, good luck too! :)

X.-Conclusion: Chapter 7.

We have explored what education is and what would be a perfect one.

Then we explored the current challenges our system faces to become one. During that we saw an example of a modern nation that had great success on the educational field Finland.

And finishing the chapter, after gathering the understanding and analyzing real world examples, I drew similarities and reached conclusions so as to create a new structure for a system aimed to achieve the goal of perfect education.

All based on current realistic means according to our technological advantage.

What are you waiting for again? Go learn the basic curriculum, go tech it, let’s start consciously building the utopia.

8.- Thoughts on the ideal society, final part: On how to transition to an utopia, putting it all together.

8.1.- The axioms, or essence, of human existence.

We have explored and understood the biological behavior of humans as individuals. All are instincts forged in genetics to drive us to survive and create slightly diverse offspring.

Once survival is assured with food, water and security, then the main core focus shifts to reaching happiness. All this as a biological mechanism to reward exploration so to have better chances of adapting to unexpected changes. This increase in chances is given by the increased amount of information we gathered in the exploration. Therefore the more combinations or order we might manage to imagine and create so to face the natural chaos.

This is what drives all human individuals. But, before all comes survival, and humans biologically need others to survive. So we can not deeply understand the system of human species without understanding the relationships between them.

The same way we can not understand physics by looking at just one atom. Even if we understood how and why the atom moves in empty space, the reality is that there are more atoms around which influence the observed one.

For that we analyzed the interactions involving more than one human. We explored and understood all the key different aspects of their interactions: physical capabilities and information management ones.

Then we used that understanding to analyze how their power dynamics work and how they use them to distribute resources while trying to guarantee survival and then optimize for happiness.

During all these, we saw a fundamental human biological trait: their brain cannot process rationally all the information it can receive. So it must find mechanisms to slow it down and try to make use of it.

From this biological, intrinsic to all individuals mechanism, remixed with the understanding of the biological reactions that fuel individual survival and species maintenance (basic survival needs and happiness), is that we can start to make sense of the interactions that regard more than one individual.

From this is how we can explain and understand all the higher level concepts humans use to label, bring to life and understand their power dynamics and resource management protocols. Or in other words, their societal existence.

We can unite, in an intellectual way, and in an identity to a group way, all the higher level concepts, regardless of their seemingly antagonistic nature at higher levels, via reasoning through these biological principles. Thus with this reaching a reconciliation and a reformulation of the apparent contradictions emergent in analysis at higher levels. Allowing us to manipulate them, use them and understand them with greater accuracy.

Everything there is to understand in human societies can be understood by the survival and evolutionary biological principles plus the human brain internal chemical mechanics which ultimately are programmed to, so far successfully, follow these principles to reach the goals.

From the fact of how humans process information we can distinguish the logical appearance of the ideas of “the variable concepts” and “the fixed concepts” that create a dynamic dance inside our brain’s chemical configurations to guide us through life, or reality.

The fixed chemical biological structures form beliefs and the dynamic plastic nature they sometimes acquire creates exploration, gives birth to dynamism.

Thus from a static-dynamic natural analysis, a fixing and varying, we can understand any human created concept.

We have done this through this book with economics, politics and ethics for example.

At the end of the day, at the beginning and the end of truth, if we want to agree and coordinate on something, we must reason on top of these static-dynamic analytical principles. Which in “reality” can be also understood as mechanics, rather than principles, if you define them in a more dynamic way. Note in this paragraph the limitations of my human brain on the intent to describe accurately, precisely, in one statement, its dual (more than one) nature.

As explained, one of the most primitive ways, in the sense of old and simple, to reconcile, understand and then use this nature inside societies, has been historically named as ethics, the labeling process of stuff as good or evil.

An ever changing dynamic nature, with a necessary static point of reference to work around. Sounds really similar to how modern day physics even works, like the theory of relativity of Albert Einstein.

Is this theory a natural real rule, or just a biased theory appearing from the internal workings of our reasoning brain processing the information? A theory created by the brain to explain what the very same brain measures, the summit of truth, a being defining itself, and doomed to be right, because he is its own inventor and invention.

I will step away from these questions for now, let’s go back to human societal workings.

We all work with the same reasoning, yet maybe, with different fixed points, fixed variables. Sharpening our ability to travel between points better and faster will make us be sharper humans, more sophisticated and advanced.

No matter what you do, these are the axioms, the essence, of human existence:

- The moment you name, the moment you fix, everything else will be perceived as if it changes.

- You can choose different angles to perceive it from. And everything will be the same reality, yet it will look different, due to the angle chosen, the variables fixed.

The key is to coordinate our dance around reality, even if looked from different angles, even if dancing different styles, in harmonious ways, without clashing.

Assume, fix, for this visual metaphor of human existence, that, whatever reality is, it is a sphere. And we are dancing around it, because we love it, because it is beautiful if you will or because we are meant to do that biologically if you are more scientific. Yet there is a bunch of us dancing around, from different angles.

Some will be dancing together, some alone, but we will all be forever dancing around that sphere. The key is to not clash or push each other against that sphere, because it hurts.

The key is to respect the sphere, because it is just like this, our common god if you like, and coordinate our dances so we contemplate together the sphere as we dance.

This is why everything might be true, if worded properly, if thought properly, because we are in the same reality, just describing it from different angles, different contexts. And, fortunately enough, or just realistically enough, the words and actions we chose don’t necessarily need to clash.

We have seen it throughout the book, in any sort of human concepts and protocols.

Good luck being human, let’s keep dancing without clashing. That is how we thrive.















8.1.1.- Another example of the human existence’s axioms. The different ways of living love.

The other day, while pondering about why people are monogamous in most of the world, I realized it was a nice example of how we humans dance around the sphere just with different styles.

Said without metaphors: It served as a perfect example on how we all describe the same reality but with different points of view, different words, different contexts yet that mold and describe ultimate concepts or realities we all share.

Personally, I’ve never practiced monogamy. In modern times this is widely understood with the meaning of having just one romantic partner and bonded, necessarily too, not by just romance but also by the sexual exclusivity for each other.

I logically thought, since I had the ability to get horny, that monogamy was not natural. My thought process was simple, we have the desire to have sex with multiple people, yet some eventually constrain it to only one, thus, as it is a byproduct of a choice and not a natural thing to do via instinct, it is anti-natural. Yet I was wrong, evil some might even say, but for sure, at the very least, I lacked a deeper understanding of the concept. Monogamy is natural, in the same way that me, a polyamorous human, also is. An actually accurate term I should have used to describe monogamy is: anti-biological. Yet humans, as seen, are not always lead by biological instinctual reactions. We dance according to our context, and our context is created by the very natural way we process the information, by the very natural way from which we try to order the chaos. Thus, natural must be.

While reflecting about this, I realized really interesting ways of describing what I felt about monogamy. Via doing economical and ideological parallelisms. Then later I realized I was just being human, like described in the previous section.

In this section you will find a critique to monogamy, and you will find it, correctly criticizing it with opposing concepts. Showing once more how seemingly opposing incompatible ideas and existences are compatible, are “coordinate-able”, if done intelligently, if analyzed from lower, deeper levels instead of from higher, more “brute“ levels.

I must add a disclaimer. Even if I do not practice monogamy, I do not think it is unnatural nor damaging. I acknowledge and observe human existence and fully understand that for some people, in their own contexts, works marvelously. For that I only have to look at my parents. They have been together for 25 years practicing monogamy and they are clearly super happy with each other. I, with my personality and context, could not do it.

The following sections are worded purposefully to feel a bit like a direct critique, almost like an attack to monogamy and to some other human concepts I mentioned. Yet this is only done to showcase better what I explained in the previous section.

How wording matters, how understanding matters, how respecting the sphere and other’s movements so not to clash against it matters. How we can fix different variables yet coordinate and understand each other, thriving, solving problems, adapting to reality.

Say no more, here it comes.

8.1.1.1.- The capitalist hate on monogamy. And the socialist one. Same reality, different fixed variables, successful coordination.

First let’s see what a more libertarian, anarchist, “freedom-prioritizer” would say against monogamy. These people have clearly fixed some variables on their lives.

Then, we will explore the same reasons but from a more socialist, controlling or protective or “empathy-prioritizer” mindset.

Then we will see that both, regardless of the different variables fixed in other areas of human existence, are trying to describe and adapt to the same concept, the same reality.

I got lazy and curious the moment I was writing this section, so I wrote the critiques with my ideas yet explained and written up by an AI:

```
MANIFESTO: Love Does Not Enclose — Against Monogamy as A Socialist Control of Instinct

We’ve been taught to equate love with sexual exclusivity. The prevailing belief says that if you truly care for someone, you will only desire them — forever, without exception. But this idea isn’t rooted in love; it’s built on fear, insecurity, and the need for control. Monogamy is not the same as love. In many cases, it becomes a structure of control disguised as emotional commitment.

Control is not the same as care. Imagine your partner dictated what you eat, when and how you eat it, who you eat with, what cutlery you use, or even how you drink water. That level of control would be seen as absurd — yet controlling sex is accepted in monogamous relationships, despite it being equally intrusive to our natural instincts.

It’s normal for people in relationships to make agreements about practical things: schedules, chores, how the home functions. That’s part of living together. But it’s an entirely different matter when someone tries to control a fundamental biological impulse like sexual desire. Wanting to control your partner’s sexuality is not the same as deciding together on household logistics. Instincts, like hunger or thirst, are elemental. Trying to limit it is a denial of the other person’s nature.

Sexual attraction does not disappear with a promise or a ring. It doesn’t vanish because of love, nor is it easily suppressed by ethics. What suppresses it is fear — and when fear enters, freedom exits. Submission replaces autonomy. Sex is part of human life. It isn’t a contractual privilege that can be negotiated away. It is not something to be granted or denied through rules and boundaries.

Monogamy often functions like a form of sexual socialism, bringing all negative effects socialism has. Daddy State promises stability and emotional security. It frames itself as being in your best interest — for the sake of the relationship. But it leads to repression, to internal conflict, to double lives, and often, to heartbreak. It demands a denial of desire, of instinct, of biological truth. 

Some humans find comfort in slavery — not literal, but the kind where freedom is exchanged for the illusion of safety. It is a voluntary kind of enslavement, but one that goes so deep it reaches into the core of who we essentially are. As Benjamin Franklin said, “Those who would give up essential liberty to purchase a little temporary safety, deserve neither liberty nor safety.” While that quote might not apply to everything, when it comes to sexual desire, it fits; surrendering your intimate freedom in exchange for emotional security is not love — it’s submission.

To love someone is to respect them, not to possess them. A partner who feels the need to forbid your desires is not protecting you; they are trying to control you because they do not feel secure without owning you. A confident, loving partner doesn’t fear your desire. They don’t need to dominate. They earn your respect by being present, honest, and free.

Imposed monogamy is not love. It is fear wearing the mask of protection. We were not born to obey sexual monopolies. We were born to live, to connect, to experience desire, and to love without cages.

Real love doesn’t require confinement. It doesn’t need legal conditions. It doesn’t say, “If you love me, you’ll never want anyone else.” Real love says, “I choose you freely, every day — even though you don’t have to choose me.” That is the essence of love.

This is the manifesto. Read it. Reflect on it. Live freely.
```

Now let’s say the same but from a modern socialist view hating on capitalism and libertarianism:

```
MANIFESTO: Love Does Not Enclose — Monogamy as Capitalist Ownership

Monogamy is often sold to us like a product. We are told that if we truly love someone, we must “own” them, keep them under lock and key, and claim exclusive rights over their body and desires. This is not love — it is the logic of capitalism, dressed up as romance. It teaches us to treat our partner like private property, something to be guarded, controlled, and negotiated over, as though a relationship were a corporate contract with endless clauses and fine print.

Under this capitalist illusion, love becomes transactional. We trade fidelity for security, desire for stability, freedom to love for the illusion of ownership. Just as capitalism thrives on scarcity and control, monogamy feeds on fear: fear of losing what we think we own, fear of not being “enough,” fear of the natural abundance of human desire. Monogamy is not love — it is the commodification of love, a social contract that mirrors the worst aspects of the market.

Control is not care. Imagine living with a boss who dictates every aspect of your life — what you eat, who you talk to, when you rest. You would call it exploitation. Yet, when this control is in your sexual activity, society tells us it’s “romantic.” Monogamy takes the raw, natural instinct of sexual desire and subjects it to the same managerial logic as a corporation. It says: “Your body, your time, your feelings belong to me.” It privatizes one of our natural instincts.

Sexual attraction, like creativity, cannot be owned or monopolized. You can’t sign a contract to make it disappear. Capitalism tries to turn everything into property — land, labor, ideas — and monogamy extends that logic into our most intimate selves. It tells us to repress our desires for the sake of “the relationship,” the same way workers are systematically coerced to repress their needs for the sake of “the company.” Repression always breeds resentment, double lives, black insecure markets outside of legality and eventual collapse.

Monogamy is sexual capitalism. It sells stability like a false product: promising happiness while quietly demanding the sacrifice of instinct and autonomy. It enforces scarcity — the idea that your partner’s love and attention is a resource you must hoard, guard, and defend. It creates a market of jealousy and competition, where your value depends on being “the only one,” rather than being freely chosen. Like capitalism, it teaches us to measure worth in ownership and exclusivity, instead of freedom and mutual respect.

Some people accept this system, just as some accept exploitation at work, thinking it’s the only way to survive. But this is not liberation — it’s a self-imposed form of servitude. So long as we believe that love requires ownership, we remain trapped in the ideology of private property.

Karl Marx once said: “The property-owning class and the class of the proletariat represent the same human self-alienation.” Applied to love, this means that turning our partners into property alienates us from our own capacity to love freely. When we enforce control, we do not connect — we dominate. We reproduce the same oppressive structures that alienate workers from their labor, only now in our most intimate spaces.

To love is to resist the capitalist logic of ownership. A partner who demands control over your desire is not loving you — they are treating you like a resource they must guard. True love does not need contracts, conditions, or monopolies. A strong partner does not fear your freedom. They stand with you as an equal, not as a manager of your instincts.

Imposed monogamy is not love. It is a capitalist cage, built on fear and control. We were not born to sign emotional contracts. We were born to live collectively, to share abundance, to love without turning each other into property.

Real love does not say, “If you love me, you’ll never want anyone else.” Real love says, “I choose you freely, every day — even though you are not mine to own.” That is the liberation of love.

This is the manifesto. Read it. Reflect. Break free from the capitalist chains of monogamy.
```

Enough AI, back to my words.

As you can see, they both are talking about the same reality of that love, a kind of 2 people relationship to live life together, requires human agreement, coexistence and coordination.

Both criticize until which extent these required agreements are ethical to make. Abstracted away from ideologies, they are trying to answer: Should we agree on controlling our couple’s natural sexual desire?

And both, abstracted away from ideologies, answer that no, we should not control it.

Reality, however, is more complex than any reasoning derived from fixed ideological variables can describe.

There are contexts where monogamy is really useful for a society. Where its presence, due to the context the society lives in, brings more freedom or happiness than the one that sexually takes away. This is true not only at societal levels, but also couple-wise levels.

Some couples will be happier being monogamous not because they enjoy controlling others, or because they have trust issues and fear abandonment, but just because it is the best option for their current situation. Like imagine a couple where they are very old, why would they bother in finding other sexual or love partners if both likely have sexual desires pretty much turned off.

To be honest I’m not the best at finding examples of when monogamy is benefitial, my polyamorous instinct finds it hard to imagine. But I’m sure there must be, otherwise it would not be as present.

Fortunately, I’ve started feeling interest and I’ve started reading other people’s thoughts. Among them I’m reading Robert Michels’ book: Political Parties: A Sociological Study of the Oligarchical Tendencies of Modern Democracy. And there it was explained beautifully that, for example, monogamy gives a man greater assurances that his children will be his and from none other. In cultures where being the father of someone or the kid of someone is very important, like in dynasties, for their social coordination, monogamy might be an essential part of culture to assure a non-chaotic functioning of society.

Anyway, this chapter is not meant to discuss on if we should be monogamous or not according to our current modern context. That is something that each of us, thinking about our contexts, will have to figure out.

I just wanted to emphasize how people, with different variables fixed, can still coordinate and discuss the same topics without necessarily clashing. In the texts showcased, we saw how people with seemingly antagonistic points of view about human economical coordination, libertarians and socialists, could agree on not being monogamous, which is just another type of human coordination. Therefore revealing the deeper, lower level nature of the problem when analyzed from different parts of overlapping spectra at higher level dimensions. The problem was actually how to handle agreements and coordination on human sexual relations.

If we had just bothered to analyze everything from the context, from the fixed variables, of economical coordination protocols, even though we would have talked about coordination and we can reach similar conclusions using meanings related to the coordination action, we would have not reached full agreement because we would be fixing too much variables, even incorrect ones, like thinking of economic coordination instead of the real deeper other topic of coordination, sexual and romantic coordination, we were actually discussing.

With these protocols of love analysis I wanted to showcase how reality can always be more complex than what any ideology based thinking can describe it as. And the potential risks of creating higher levels, avoidable, conflicts, by fixing too much variables. As seen, two poliamorous people can think the other person’s text is worthless because they might be reading it from “a bias”, a thought process where too much variables were fixed while trying to understand a part of reality which, even if overlapping and similar, is different.

In this case we analyzed a system of two humans solving a coordination problem in a relation so to enjoy and share their sexual and romantic lives together. Green circle in the image.

Which, as seen, it can be understood as a relation of desires or instincts and economics. If you fix yourself with the fixed ideas of any of the capitalist or socialist protocols mentioned, you will likely just miss the deeper nature and components of what you are analyzing: humans relation with love and sexual desire.

From the image, your thought would have wandered around the red area and the intersection of it with the green area if you remained fixed in the assumptions of socialism, and you would have completely missed and never reached the green part that goes far beyond an economical analysis. Therefore, limiting yourself in the ways you can sail in this blue sea of reality we have on the picture, so as to satisfy your goals, order your chaos, in more diverse and versatile ways.
Ultimately, in more complex and sophisticated ways that can avoid conflict with your neighbors. Like agreeing on non-monogamy even if having different economical ideas, fixed variables. Not only this but the realization of common ground, as explained in the chapter of world peace, promotes to not to perceive humans as “the other”. But someone more like us, like our group. Further promoting more sophisticated dialogue and less chaotic coordination.

Note that, starting the analysis from ideology is not incorrect perse. If you start thinking about it with both ideologies, one at a time, then draw similarities, you will be able to realize the points in common, which fortunately are very handy for analyzing the system at its root, on its nature. Thanks to it being analyzed from different yet complementary points of view.

Here we see again what I’ve mentioned along the book, we should use labels because they are necessary, but not as a truth, but a guide towards it. And for similar reasons this is why names do not really matter that much, what mattes is the thinking capabilities and understanding.

This is precisely why we should not be proud of ideological confrontation, we should praise thinking, talking, putting intellectual effort in finding common ground and then coordinate in the seek of deeper truths better aligned with the reality we share. We must strive for and we should crave for intelligence and deeper analysis. Especially with the people who might have fixed different variables in similar aspects of life, because then, we can unveil a greater understanding and sailing skills through reality.

Keeping the previous poetry, we must keep dancing, whatever style we prefer, without clashing, around the sphere. Let’s keep the party of life going.

8.1.2.- A more modern version of good and evil, of left and right.

In modern times, when solving complex problems at higher levels of societal structures, people use 2 sides: left and right. Sometimes the figure of the center appears, but it has been mostly anecdotal.

These terms are vague on purpose, they are like good and evil, terms that shapeshift across history. What is good now might be evil in 20 years, what was left-wing 20 years ago now might be right wing.

Ultimately it is because of the human biology we explained. These words are just labels we use to commonly agree on what to do in the current context.

As time passes and context changes, different labels might be used upon the same idea.

We already know the common ground here, the objective definition of good and evil:

``Good and bad are those things that have seemed to grant this better or worse likelihood of survival and happiness according to an individual or group of people’s personalities and their nature around them.``

Left and right are exactly the same. It is just that these words are often used when talking about political and economical solutions to the problems of coordinating power dynamics and resource management.

We have seen over and over again that these labels are incomplete. They always simplify reality. So here I will propose labels that do not, or at least, that resonate closer to our nature.

Labels that hopefully help us think better. Yet, we must not be proud of being guided by labels, we should aim for taking action based on dialogue with others, not by just labels. We must  be guided by dialogue, specially dialogue with those tending to use opposing labels.

Now, before proposing my labels, let me explain something important to understand why I think they can help us think better.

8.1.2.1.- A key difference, correct and incorrect answers are not the same as good and bad answers.

So correct and incorrect are things that are scientifically correct, that can be concluded by the laws of physics or any science, by anyone, anywhere, anytime.

Things like, assuming you are on Earth’s surface and have human strength:

If I throw the spear upwards, it will fall downwards.

A scientific fact.

Knowledge can be labeled scientific if it follows the following principles:

- It can always be used to predict the future.
- It can always be replicated or discovered by anyone or any group.

So, solutions like, if I’m thirsty drinking water will make me not thirsty is a correct solution. Is it a good solution though? In this case yes, because it promotes your survival and even happiness.

Is throwing a spear to hunt a deer when hungry a correct solution to the problem of not being able to eat it? It depends, will the deer be dead or injured enough so you can physically control it? Then it is correct, if the deer scapes, it is incorrect.

Is it good or bad? Well, that will depend on if hunting that deer is needed for your survival or if it makes you happy.

But what about the deer? It is clearly bad for it.

Actions that include more than 1 individual are not always objectively good or evil. It depends on the point of reference. Because we have then two brains processing reality, thus what for one is a static part defined as truth, for the other one it might also be a static part but fixed as something false. From this extra bit of information we gather new extra combinations. When there was one individual it was either one or zero: 0 or 1. Now we have two individuals and each of them can be zero or one (false or truth), thus we got 4 possible combinations: 0 and 0, 0 and 1, 1 and 0, 1 and 1.

We must understand that, in the same way correct and incorrect are the basic labels we use to guide logic and science from the perspective of one observer. Good and evil are this very same concept of basic labels. Which we use to guide the judging process on actions that pertain to more than 1 individual.

Generally speaking, labels we apply when we have more than a single being interacting in opposing ways to each solve one problem or both a common one.

Thus, to label a solution we must take into account 2 positions, the individual and the other. Or others.

There are 4 combinations possible as seen:

- Good for individual, good for others. (Example: Hunts a deer and shares it with others.)
- Good for individual, bad for others. (Example: Starves others by hiding the hunted deer.)
- Bad for individual, good for others. (Example: Kills an individual which was killing others.)
- Bad for individual, bad for others.  (Example: Nuclear bombing each other.)

There are 2 dimensions, 2 variables, the individual point of existence and the other point of existence. Whereas with correct and incorrect there is only one, whether it is true or not. 

Combinations for logical conclusions:

- It is true. (Example: If I throw a spear upwards it falls downwards.)
- It is false. (Example: If I throw a spear upwards it becomes a speaking banana and teaches me to be a ninja master.)

Fixing some variables is perceiving something as good or bad. It does not necessarily mean it is correct or good and incorrect or bad, but that the analyzer chooses to perceive it as so.

That election of label just marks an election, and nothing else in the logic realm.

Good and evil, even if they are basic labels, they are not a logical deduction. They will always be subjective, depending on the observer.

From the point of view of this poor deer we have been mentioning, all is bad, regardless of correct or incorrect statements, we have been trying to kill him over and over again.

Question people who say that answers to social problems are the correct thing to do or the right thing to do. Like if it was logical, a guarantee. They might maliciously or accidentally think they are intelligent enough so to be an omniscient god.

Also don’t just trust those who say, this is the good thing to do, they can also be wrong, as good and bad are just perceptions, our perceived as most correct guess when fixing variables. This is why dialogue is key when coordinating with others. Because jut one human brain easily leads to more inefficient and inadequate conclusions in matters of increasing complexity involving multiple beings.

I think understanding this distinction can be helpful to promote dialogue.

Every time I say something is good or bad, I mean it this way, as a time constrained perception, not as an assured reality.

Now you might have realized we are severely relying on using a one dimensional approach (left or right wing) to guide our complex, 2 dimensional dilemma, of organizing societies of more than one individual.

Therefore, we are tending to miss other parts of reality and this is limiting the complexity and quality of our solutions to problems at a species level. Thus here I propose:

8.1.2.2.- The new left and right, a two dimensional and natural approach.

Finally here they are, the new left and right are:

1.- Centralized / Decentralized.
2.- Static / Dynamic.

These two pairs should aid modern humans to better analyze problems according to their two dimensional societal nature and not according to a one dimensional ideological limited analysis.

Aiding them to only fix the variables who are necessary in each moment and reduce the tendency to oversimplify realty, a.k.a. fix too much variables at once.

The reason behind this is that these pairs are chosen based on biological human principles that are correct and incorrect.

They are not based on ideas of matters involving multiple individuals which can be good or bad.

Let’s explain the pairs.

Centralized vs Decentralized:

A solution is centralized when:

More variables can be fixed per user with power than in the decentralized alternative.

And a solution is decentralized when:

Less variables can be fixed per user with power than in the centralized alternative.

This way, we promote to start discussing with labels that align scientifically with reality.

The first reason on why they align is because of the presence on their definition of the biological information processing functioning of our brain. It respects and acknowledges the human problem solving method of the fixed variable resolution technique.

And second, it is scientific because of the logical part of it. As the variables handled can be named and counted, a.k.a. measured. And the same can be said as per users that will hold power. So there can not be an arbitrary, feelings-based dispute over what is a more centralized or decentralized solution, you jut have to think and count the factors.

Static vs Dynamic:

A solution is static when:

Includes more variables which become fixed and/or for longer time than in the dynamic alternative.

And dynamic when:

Includes less variables which become fixed and/or for lesser time than in the static alternative.

With these we complement the previous pair. We do not only have to decide who handles more variables, but how many and for how long.

So now we have encapsulated in our labels all components of a living being’s reality: being capable (power), time and amounts.

As said, time is measurable, amount of variables is measurable, capability of action is measurable, so these labels are scientific. Thus they should promote a more critical thinking process, even if requiring the humanly unavoidable mere existence of a label, of a fixed variable.

Both label pairs can be used together or separately to judge solutions to problems. Leading to a more human-nature-aligned decision taking. Taking into account our shared reality instead of abusively, or in a brute way, prioritizing individual ones.

As you might have noticed, I’ve clearly used these labels when analyzing resource management protocols in chapter 5.

The main goal of someone who is truly critical is to first, if desired, use labels like these ones to start the thinking. This is basically step one of thinking like an engineer: define stuff with names, adjectives etc. Then, actually complete all the other steps of thinking like an engineer.

Sure, again rational thinking can’t always be done, for example if resources are truly limited. I just hope that these new labels can be useful for modern humans to start their path into critical thinking.

These 2 pairs of labels presented are just a less biased, zero-biased due to their scientific nature I would dare to say, start.

As you have more options with this 2-dimensional approach, more meanings can be uncovered in the initial understanding. Whereas using traditional left and right, which is just 1 pair of variables, leads to a poorer initial understanding.

Anyway, until we get to the point where everyone just thinks like an engineer and people do not start conflict just by shallow poorer labels, these 2 pairs should serve as a fresh more efficient start.

To reiterate and conclude this section, remember, labels are not truth, just a guide, a compass, but we must move using the compass to seek solutions, we must not stay where we are forever.

8.2.- Patterns on answers and why democracy, for now.

Earlier in the book, in chapter 4, I mentioned that I think the best power dynamics protocol is democracy. But I did not explain much in detail why. That was because it was harder to explain without presenting to you the 2 label pairs (2 dimensions) from the previous section.

As a brief curiosity, the reasons that made this harder were the following:

If we approach power from a more ethical, good and evil, one dimensional, wording, we risk leaving the nature of pure capability out of the thinking table. If we think jut with one label pair, we risk missing deeper complexities. Good and evil imply the existence of the other as we saw in a recent previous section. If we think only in the dimension of coexistence, and we are only used to one dimensional analysis, then we risk omitting the consideration of full power. One where the other does not really affect in practice the execution of your desires and impulses.

Precisely because of this deeper nature too, starting to understand it from an analytical framework of thought is also less optimal. As full power does not need to be understood, it does not need to ask for permission to exist, it jut needs to be exerted. So first I wanted to lay out a display of the analytical process with the resource management dilemma, where thinking plays more of a crucial role, and does it more intuitively, which allows me to introduce the framework of thinking in a smoother, yet longer, way.

In the analysis of economics (resource management), because we start from an agreement point of view, the agreement of money usage, the pure power realm is easily and directly discarded in the analysis, because we start theorizing from a consensus, therefore not a matter of absolute power. Making it a more suitable topic so to better start familiarizing oneself with new frameworks of thinking. Like the one I’m proposing, centralized/decentralized, static/dynamic.

However, in human existence, power comes first, resource management later. Therefore I chose to present those in that order on this book. In individual matters, in the sense that the individual is the one who feels them, the matters to present where happiness and intelligence. And then I chose the social matters. As a curious fact, that is the structure that my head followed when writing all this. First displaying and understanding the pieces that build the individual, and then doing the same with the things that each individual being a pice builds, society.

I realized that this intuitive order of presentation exposes a natural dynamic. In the same way I think the individual human is first guided by happiness and then intelligence starts arising and intertwining, in the societal scope, the human is first guided by power dynamics and then resource management starts playing a role in a similar intertwined way.

Therefore, a pure analysis of just the political or jut the economical realm will be incomplete.

Curiosities aside about why I chose this order for presenting the concepts, let’s start the analysis.

Democracy can be very efficient just like libertarianism, but in power terms.

I started to see a trend, the solutions that tend to work better have these 2 traits:

1.- Decentralization via minimization of variables handled per individual with action potential.

2.- Maximization of the intelligence of the individual with action potential. Increasing its dynamism.

First, we already saw in chapter 5 why libertarianism abides number one, but does democracy abide by it?

If applied ideally, it does. At least better than the other popular alternatives like dictatorships or Oligarcracies. But anyway, if I want to get deeper into the explanation I must then clearly define what I mean by democracy.

8.2.1.- Building the definitions of the most famous power dynamics protocols.

Here are some, incomplete for now, definitions:

- Dictatorship: when there is one leader with a bunch of allies, all of them under the same group, always managing the State. No other group is allowed to aspire to manage the State (the monopoly on the use of violence).

- Oligarcracy: when there is more than one group, each with their respective leaders and interconnected internal management structures. The groups alternate between each other, every now and then, which one of them manages the State. For any other emergent group that might aspire to manage the State they need to be first approved by groups already capable of managing the State and to follow similar internal management structures to the ones the existing groups hold.

- Democracy: it is like an oligarcracy but there is no need for the existing groups’ approval to create new groups. Nor to follow similar internal management structures. The only requisite to create a new group is that any amount of 2 or more citizens, just because they are citizens, can create a group to aspire to manage the State. Each group internally managed as they want as long as the management solely depends on the effort of the members belonging to that group.

- Anarchism: There are groups, but there is no State. There is no monopoly on violence, nor violence, ideally. The groups organize with each other without the use and the fear of external violence.

Let’s start with anarchism, I already explained why I think it works worse than democracy. Because we are not intelligent enough and technologically advanced enough.

If it were possible, it would be better than democracy as the lack of needing violence clearly signals levels of abuse that are insignificant. Therefore that society would be composed of individuals who can be very happy and are very intelligent. All traits of the best natural way for societies and individuals to thrive.

Ideally, in anarchism power is not abused. But in modern reality power can lead to abuse and that is why all the previous definitions were incomplete.

As you can see, the fundamental traits that define the power dynamics protocols are who and how they are allowed to get and manage power. The greater the amount of people, or groups of people who can get and manage power, the more so called democratic the protocol is.

Originally, the name democracy come from the following. As societies are build with people and therefore the unit, the elemental source of power, is each individual in the people, in the nation, in the “demos”, that means “the people” in Greek. And “-cracy”, comes from the Greek word “kratos”, which means “power” or “rule.” The power of the people, the democracy.

The more correctly a power dynamics protocol reflects the aggregated will of the people, the more democratic is.

Thinking it with the new framework, if we want a power dynamics protocol that behaves like the people would do, by logical deduction, the only way to do so is by abiding the minimization via decentralization of variables handled per individual with action potential rule. Because only achieving greater decentralization we can achieve a behavior that better reflects the aggregated sum of people’s actions without losing too much nuances due to noisy information channels. So, democracy by the mere need derived from its definition, is the most dynamic power dynamics protocol involving a State.

We could say, in a classical way, that dictatorships are the least democratic protocol. But, as I’ve been explaining, I think that framework has limitations, and deeper truths can be unveiled with the new framework proposed.




Or, if you fancy saying the same but from the opposite perspective:



Continuing, we must realize that, as in physics, power is not always just action, it can generate or find an opposing power, a reaction.

So let’s now understand how each protocol deals with reactions in order to actually complete the definitions.

Note that reactions might lead to an abuse, but not necessarily, as agreements can occur. And by the way, here it is where most of humans hit their analytical limit. As they try to understand power from an ethical perspective, as they use the word abuse, implying a good and an evil. Even though some analysis are actually correct and very useful, they will limit the human using them by reducing the amount of people they will be able to talk to in order to reach any kind of useful conclusions over power dynamic protocols.

Anyway, even if you analyze the matter from an ethical perspective, the need for taking into account the reaction forces in the definition logically follows too. So, this being clarified, let’s go.

Completing the definitions: Democracy.

The definition of democracy should be completed with stating a complete separation, in all directions of the capabilities (powers) of the State, between its 3 different natural branches: executive (manages resources and enforces law), legislative (creates, destroys and shapes laws), judicial (judges when conflict arises as per what is dictated in law).

A complete separation in all directions means that all 3 powers are completely independent from one another, this means that they do not influence one another. That is why I chose the wording separation of directions, because forces applied in separate directions do not influence each other. There are multiple methods you can use to implement this behavior in the institutions that conform the State, they will be discussed later.

If you pay attention these 3 powers are the natural components of human action: muscle (executive power), rules for information processing and analysis (legislative power, the laws are like the neurons of a State fixing variables) and a process to solve problems when contradictory information and muscle move (judicial power, which is like the reasoning process of a brain).

But, why is separating powers essential to complete the definition of democracy? Because once one of the groups is chosen to manage and be the State, if the power of the State is not separated and controlled, then its monopoly on violence, thus unmatched power, can be used for whatever the group wants. And that whatever, for example, can be the complete change on the power dynamics protocol in use, setting other mechanics and rules, like oligarchic or dictatorial ones.

Therefore if we want to create a democratic protocol we must have a separation of powers that control each other with equal force, so there is no unmatched power that can change the rules whenever it fancies. That equal force that controls and that is given to each separated natural power can be, for example, the required support of the people of a nation. So now we would have a system that not only puts the forces pointing in different directions, but one that, if for any reason any force deviates and clashes against another, they will self-nullify or self-destroy due to having the same amount of force.

Note that, a democracy without these limits would be weak and unstable, as per mentioned, if the group managing the State wishes, could just transition to another power dynamics protocol.

Please refrain from labeling this potential dynamic arising from the incomplete definition a good or evil mechanic. As you might have noticed I have not used them nor the word abuse, which by its previous definition implies some good and some evil. That will depend on who you ask, likely the group with the power would consider this action good, others that might not agree with all its decisions will consider it evil. Just remember, at the end of the day, we can achieve deeper, more useful truths without using these labels.

Therefore now we can see, that by the very nature of the State, due to its unmatched power, we have to separate it and give each of the separations equal force if we want for our power dynamics protocol to be a democratic one that lasts.

Personally, another intuitive understanding for completing the definition of democracy is: a power dynamics protocol that results in the most delta neutral partition of the powers within the State, ideally this one being zero.

For those of you who do not know what delta neutral means. In math delta is usually used as another word for difference, it is usually written with the Greek letter delta (this one →  Δ). It just means taking the difference of 2 things, so delta neutral means that the difference is neutral, nothing, zero. This means that if we take the amount of power given to each partition of the power of a State, and we subtract them with one another, the result will be 0. Therefore, balanced.

The less neutral is the delta, the greater is the chance that, by random events of nature and society or by calculated events from groups in a society, oligarchic or dictatorial power dynamics can be set.

Just by pure force mechanics and statistical reasoning, by the pure changing will of the power holders, we need to complete the definition of a democracy with the separation of powers and the complete independence from one another.

Some will argue, and I think they are statistically right, that we need the separation and independence of powers in a democracy in order to minimize the potential yet assured abuse from the State to the people when their interests are not the same.

The argumentation goes as follows: Any uncontrolled power, given long enough time or just by existing, ends up in abusive tendencies. I consider this an interesting and very strong argumentation, because in all human history so far, this seems to be the tendency. However, in theory, a total power can chose not to abuse. Therefore I’m not a strong supporter, even though I support it and consider it a functional reasoning process, of constructing a definition and understanding of democracy from this ethical point of view. I consider it ethical because if you are considering abuse as a factor, you are implying a good and an evil. Someone harming other (evil) in the benefit of oneself (a good).

The argumentation considers that it is natural, and easier, for a living being to just abuse as long as it is not faced by an equal, or threatening enough, force. In similar words, as seen, a being can abuse as long as it can control the chaos arising from its abuse.

Again, all are likelihoods, there is a chance that an unmatched power remains non-abusive for a long time. Yet that is not the tendency as per human history so far, thus we should not act every day as if it was, because then, per sheer statistics of nature, we would be wrong most of the time. This is mainly why I support this flow of thoughts even if I do not consider it the pure foundation that should be used to define democracy.

Personally I think this tendency stems from the complexity of our societies, as per the amount of individuals, and the subjective nature of happiness. We have so many people and so many desires that makes us happy that to coordinate them all using non-conflicting forces is impossible for our current degree of intelligence. Therefore, abstracting our thoughts from this to reach deeper truths is very hard.

On top of that, though at more fundamental levels which I do agree as fundamental, the argumentation follows with that creating chaos, disorder, is literally more physically easy, it requires less effort. I agree until here. The, the argumentation says that as long as a living being can still live in the chaos, it will do so, by inertia. Unless faced with another force bearer being, a competitor, that makes the first being not able to successfully exists with the chaos to satisfy its needs. The way I disagree with this is that I consider it incomplete, I do think living beings might just not stay in the chaos by inertia. What distinguishes living beings from inert ones is that we “machines” with ordering capabilities.

Even with this debate apart, what I will explain still holds. So, then, because of these natural tendencies, even if somehow we start with democratic traits of power access and management as the ones defined on the previous incomplete definition, if a society just incorporates them to its power dynamics and nothing more, the power will tend to be every time reduced in smaller and smaller amounts of groups with greater and greater amounts of power. Because whichever group controls the State, which is an absolute power, if it controls all its parts, at some point, it will fall into the natural tendency of making it easier for them to follow its own interest and goals.

And, making it easier for them means that it will eventually require altering the power dynamics protocol so it is easier for the groups controlling the State to keep it, resulting in the application of similar dynamics described in the oligarcracy or even in the dictatorship incomplete definitions.

So we have seen that to actually define and therefore create a democracy we must take into account the actions and reactions mechanics and constrain then in such a way that they do not break other parts of the definition.

You can reach this conclusion, as seen, via just thinking about pure power and forces or via thinking about ethical interests and forces.

Completing the definitions: Dictatorship.

Now let’s go to dictatorship. How does it handle the potential reactions and how should we define this management in order to keep the definition consistent?

At a State level, dictatorships, by an ideal definition do not have this problem. As they do not allow any competitor and they have the all mighty power of the State.

However if we step away from the definition and ideas realm, in reality they likely have competitors that have to be silenced.

As, as seen with the limited variables that can be handled per human, similar to the critique to communism, a reduced group of people can not accurately rule and govern with the same interests as every single human on a big society they rule for, or rule over.

Thus we encounter a clash and potential for abuse. Now, if the protocol for power dynamics must be a dictatorship, then we can include in its realistic and complete definition the use of methods to neutralize any potentially strong enough opposing power. These methods can be imprisonment, censorship, public executions, silent murdering, the modern social media defamation campaign, economical bribery to corrupt initially real opposition... among others.

The ruling group (elite) will tend to chose the silencing act who creates the more manageable chaos according to the intelligence of the ruling group compared to the abused and repressed group. The more intelligent and strong they are compared to the abused being, usually the people, the more severe and chaos tending the abuses they can make, like public executions. Elites, by mere definition, are way smaller in number compared to the people, so in practice the abuse amount and methods’ severity are proportional to the difference in intelligences of the elite with the people. The greater the difference in intelligences, the more severe the abuses.

Completing the definitions: Oligarcracy.

Let’s now complete the definition of oligarcracy.

oligarcracies, ideally, do not really mind about reactions either. As the groups that form them are the only ones who allow or not the creation of other groups. They, by definition, can’t just abuse in any way desired as dictators do, yet they just have to follow some rules based on a consensus agreed with their elite peers. And, if any other group tries to emerge, they will directly or indirectly force him to follow those rules and fall in the elite’s consensus.

As you might have noticed, for the very same reasons, the completion of the definition is the same as in the dictatorship. Due to the impossibility of making the whole society have the same interests as the ruling elites, they will have to neutralize the ones who differ. Usually, due to existing multiple groups that require consensus, the neutralization process is less direct, or more sophisticated than in dictatorships. Because the groups have to agree, reach a consensus, the methods for reactions’ neutralizations must be more complex as they must align with the intelligences and power of each distinct group in the elite.

A way in which oligarchies neutralize opposing and revolutionary groups is to assure that if they emerge, then they try to corrupt them via economics and making them become non-revolutionary groups by linking their economic funding to public funds, a.k.a. tax payer money collected and controlled by the all-mighty power of the State.

Then, leveraging that any human organization at large scales functions as an oligarchy, as Robert Michels observed last century, they jut need to bribe the leader or the little most influential people inside the new revolutionary movement and hope for them to be able to fool their followers into submission. It work pretty well. But, if for any reason the follower are not fooled, well then it does not work and other methods will have to be used.

The money they used does not really need to just be tax payer money, it can also be money mainly controlled and/or greatly influence by the already existing groups that can aspire to control the State, the elites. This is what I meant by interconnected internal management structures at the initial definitions. In this case, I’m explaining an example of economical interconnected structure.

And, as the last nuance, they do not really need to bribe the key revolutionaries with money, they can also threat with violence at the mafia style, social defamation, or any other silencing technique already mentioned in the dictatorship part.

This way, leaders of opposing groups that act by reaction can be bought and slowly the leaders themselves silence or trick their followers into eventually making less or even no opposing force.

Completing the definitions: Finale.

And finally let’s complete the definitions of oligarcracies and dictatorships stating that in them, there can not be a complete separation of powers. In dictatorships none at all, and in Oligarcracies there might be some, but not complete.

This is because the powers of the State can not be fully or even slightly separated. Because if so the degree of freedom that that separation of power brings can lead to emerging groups that can not be controlled by the existing one/s.

Thus democracy is not only defined by the people’s capability to create groups with a high degree of freedom, but also from the fact that it tries, by definition and its assured survival, to reduce to a minimal any abuse of power.

Because in a system where people can freely create groups, but once one group is elected has all power, it is just really energetically easy to eventually centralize group creation mechanics and lead to an oligarcracy or tyranny (dictatorship) as we saw.

This is actually one of the core reasons why some nations allow gun ownership to their citizens, so to counterbalance this natural risk of powerful entities, like a State, to slowly centralize in faulty systems and start being abusive without control. There are other methods not involving guns, like educating people and designing your institutions accurately, we will talk about them later. As someone born in a non-guns country, I found the argumentation interesting, I will leave it here for all those who have been born in places like mine.

Anyway, more curious thoughts apart, here I leave the final definitions:

- Dictatorship: when there is one leader with a bunch of allies, all of them under the same group, always managing the State. No other group is allowed to aspire to manage the State (the monopoly on the use of violence).

- Oligarcracy: when there is more than one group, each with their respective leaders and interconnected internal management structures. The groups alternate between each other, every now and then, sometimes even the people vote it in elections, on which one of them manages the State. For any other emergent group that might aspire to manage the State they need to be first approved by groups already capable of managing the State and to follow similar internal management structures to the ones the existing groups hold.

- Democracy: it is like an oligarcracy but there is no need for the existing groups’ approval to create new groups. Nor to follow similar internal management structures. The only requisite to create a new group is that any group, 2 citizens or more, just because they are citizens, can create a group to aspire to manage the State. Each group internally managed as they want as long as the management only depends on the effort of the members of that group.

- Anarchism: There are groups, but there is no State. There is no monopoly on violence, nor violence, ideally. The groups organize with each other without the use and the fear of external violence.

Note that I did not bother yet in completing or making more nuanced my understanding of anarchism. This is a practical choice, my time and brain power is limited and I prefer to focus on other protocols that actually exist today and so far make doable sense to my thinking process. As I grow and I learn and think more details about everything, including anarchism, I will keep refining the book with them as I always do.

For example, I’m currently reading Robert Michels’ study on the oligarchic tendencies of democratic groups. To be honest, I think, for now, due to cognitive limits, even democratic systems eventually land in the alternation in power of 2 or little more main parties (groups). Maybe this is linked to the good and evil, yes or no, mindset we currently use. Maybe, if we adopt the 2 dimensional approach, in democratic nations, there will be 4 main parties.

Anyway, this does not affect democracy, as it does not mean that there will be lot of option to chose from, it just means that, if there is a need for a new option or to replace an existing one, it can be done with ease by the people.

8.2.2.- Why democracy, for now.

Now that we know the definitions under I which construct this book. Let me explain why I think we should aim for democracy.

8.2.2.1.- Why not-s.

Why not dictatorships?

I will start explaining it by tackling why I do not prefer dictatorships.

They are worse as they lack dynamism thus it is less adaptive, which makes satisfying human needs harder in ever changing environments, specially in ones who do it quickly.

Furthermore, dictatorships tend to be very centralized by nature, thus there is a high chance they are handled too many variables to manage. Just as in my critique to communism in the economics part. This lack of enough intelligence to handle so many variables likely leads to inefficient actions, as abusive behavior, which is not good for the majority by definition, as the dictating group is a minority. Yeah, zero abuse is always impossible, yet we must minimize the chances of it, not increase them.

I do not mean dictatorships can not work. Dictators can still make good decisions. And if they do it consistently, they will likely face no power tackling back against them.

As I always say it depends on the analytical context. Yet, in bigger contexts, those of long-term tendency terms, dictatorships are more static and more centralized, precisely the traits that obstruct intelligent individuals to flow freely and solve problems while and for adapting to future challenges.

Hence, the chances of a dictatorship adapting are lower, they are not the rule, they are in tendencies terms, the exception. And we should not aim to behave like we live in a continuous exception, because then we will be statistically wrong most of the time.

Why not oligarcracies?

The critique to oligarcracy is basically the same. Yet, as oligarcracies have a greater number of groups with a slightly greater variety, it has a more dynamic nature and it is less centralized.

Because of this, it will statistically function better than a dictatorship. Still, it is not as decentralized and as dynamic as a democracy.

However, as oligarcracies are a more sophisticated and complex system, you can craft more complex and sophisticated arguments on why they should exists. We will explore them now. Like the ideas behind plutocracies and technocracies.

But, all of them can not escape the truth of its more static and centralized nature, qualities that, as explained all along and repeating myself, obstruct intelligent individuals to flow freely and solve problems while and for adapting to future challenges.

They will, for some time, escape that truth yet they can not escape it forever. This deeper static and centralized nature, by the natural forces of human existence, will at some point stop being enough, and both dictatorships and oligarcracies will have to be, as software engineers say, deprecated.

Even though human nature is hierarchical and an authority is needed, as human societies change with its natural cycle: people are born, die and teach each other along the way. As that process executes, if humans do not get extinguished and we find ways of successfully storing the information taught, which we seem to be good at, the complexity of our societies will grow.

We can not escape forever the ever growing complexity of wisdom, which eventually requires decentralization and dynamism to arrange.

This is the fundamental argument that make these protocols eventually not functional. Which is, in practice, a gamble which its odds get worse the more time it passes. As you can not measure, you can not predict, if you can not predict, your ability to solve problems and adapt decreases over time.

This fundamental cycle of our existence brings the end of centralized and static protocols, slowly testing them out, creating friction, with each new generation of humans. New beings, with slightly or completely different characteristics and birth-environments will be born which will lead to lots of completely or slightly different desires that will need to be arranged all over again.

The complexity of the task does not end there. These new beings, because of another human trait, the one of teaching the new generations old lessons, will likely inherit greater, more complex wisdom, for example, technological progress related knowledge. A higher starting point of complexity in their intellectual journey, which, will unavoidably create friction with the simpler social structures and norms created for the lower complexity starting points of the previous generations.

The friction will and must be resolved, and societies with power dynamics protocols that are more centralized and static, will create more pressure and explosions, in the shape of societal violence, stress, visible or silent misery generally speaking, when exposed to this unavoidable friction.

Newer technologies, more complex wisdom reflected in a deeper understanding of the universe, which usually allows for more of us to exist taking usage of our natural resources, which makes no other thing but to make the system even more complex, putting even more burden on top of these simpler more centralized and static systems.

Overall, as long as we keep fucking, preserving and teaching knowledge, our societies will do no other thing but to increase in complexity. And there will be a point where these more centralized and static protocols will just not be enough.

Therefore, if we want to last in time, we must transition to democracy, and in a very far away future, if we figure it out, to anarchism-look-alike protocols.

If we do not do it, then conflicts, also by the very same nature of humans, will arise. And these conflicts, technical or social, in the same way that society is now more complex, they will be more complex to solve too. Whenever that happens, there is chance, which ultimately will be a reality, that the old ologarcracies and dictatorships won’t be able to solve them.

Due to too much variable, I’m unable to predict if we are already close to that point in time. That point in time will come, however, I just do not know when. What I know is that the amount of wars in the last decades keeps being relatively the same and in the same old geographical areas. This might be signaling the limits of minimizing abuse given our current political and economical solutions.

New revolutionary technologies are being developed: CDNs, AI, and zero-knowledge cryptography which will allow for the creation of more efficient solutions. Wether centralized and static ones or dynamic and decentralized ones. I bet that, due to the increase flow of information and new trust dynamics these technologies create, they will be the key to actually make all nations step towards the next decentralization step.

The next step, without more war and extreme conflict, look like:

- Most oligarcracies will become democracies.

- Actual democracies will refine their checks-and-balances that keep the system going.

- Hard dictatorships, those that nowadays there are not even elections and are isolated from the world will transition to oligarchracies for a generation.

- Soft dictatorships will transition to a small period of half a human generation of oligarcracies. With soft dictatorships I refer to these countries which nowadays refer to themselves as democracies just because their population can vote but the same figure or party stays in power for decades and because all new candidates suddenly die, disappear or are bribed into retiring.

I predict this timeline because, thanks to the new technologies, we can learn faster and communicate better the way forward. Taking less time that the previous decentralization steps took.

However, if we do not follow this path, who knows, maybe one of the conflicts is the so famous and always around the corner World War III that extinguishes our species. That, if anything, will signal the dumbness of our species, we, human beings, with whatever biological mechanisms we had, were not able to go further.

Concluding with the argumentation against more centralized and static systems: Even though more centralized and static protocols might be the temporary solution that works now and worked in the past, sooner or later, they will stop working. As the inherited wisdom makes complexity grow. This is the ever growing complexity of wisdom curse, or blessing, humans face.

In any way, and in favor of Cheerfulism, as we have seen previously, the maximization of intelligence with a focus on happiness optimization creates several dynamics already explained in section 5.4.2 so to be optimistic regarding the the minimization of abuse, which leads to less conflict, less chaos, more predictability. Makings survival and happiness easier to execute even if we remain in dictatorships or oligarcracies.

Why not democracies?  On the gun-to-monkey weakness.

Don’t be a fool either, even if I have democratic tendencies, I acknowledge its imperfections. Don’t forget point 2 from the essential traits that protocols which work best follow:

2.- Maximization of the intelligence of the individual with action potential. Increasing its dynamism.

Decentralization and dynamism are really cool and work marvelously, yet only if given to intelligent individuals. One because only intelligent individuals can process as much variables, and second, which derives from one, because the creation and maintenance of such systems is a highly complex task on itself, requiring for its successful completion the achievement of such degree of intelligence.

A short Youtube video I love, where a guy named Osho (also known as Rajneesh), an Indian philosopher as per what the AI told me, once said:

“Democracy basically means government by the people, of the people, for the people... but the people are retarded.”

Here is a Youtube link in case you are reading this in an era where Youtube exists: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=QFgcqB8-AxE.

This emblematic quote summarizes really well the main “danger” of democracy, but, deep down, it actually summarizes the danger I’ve named right above of decentralizing and making more dynamic systems with less intelligent and dumber people.

As mentioned, these logically better systems are more complex, going no further than democracy, designing a properly functioning democratic constitution is a far more complex task than the one, if it even exits, of a dictatorship. Dictatorships do not have to deeply bother with game theory, incentives design, checks and balances, unambiguous wording etc They jut have to bother about effective organization of the State and silencing potential uprising revolts. But, as it has all the power of the State, the second to-do is not that hard. Anyway, the task of organizing a State in itself is a difficult one that a body which is centralized and static will eventually mess up as we have previously analyzed.

The danger of democracy can also be simply understood with this other popular phrase: This is like giving a gun to a monkey.

Plutocracy or technocracy, mentioned earlier, which are jut a type of oligarcracy, based their whole existence on this premise. In case you do not know, plutocracy defends the right of the wealthiest groups to control power. And technocracy defends the right of the technocrats elite to control power. Technocrats are those who know how technology works and make it progress. Curiously enough, in a system that rewards efficiency above most of things, technocrats usually end up being among the richest and both types of olgarcraciess mix, leading to a sort of plutotecnocracy.

Libertarianism, as you might have noticed, has the same “gun-to-monkey” weakness. But in the realm of economics.

As I said with socialism in resource management: Oligarcracies, or even dictatorships might be needed, but we should not be proud of them, one because they signal the untamed presence of abusive traits which promote chaos, and second because that chaos, arising from abuse and from the ever growing complexity of human wisdom, leads to limits and friction in our thriving capabilities as a species. For these two fundamental reasons we should aim and strive for systems as much decentralized and dynamic as possible, such as democracy and libertarianism, both understood under the definitions of this book, remember. 

As a currently controversial take, nations that fall under dictatorial or oligarchic regimes do so, in part, because of their and their neighbors’ lack of greater intelligence. Wether of politicians or citizens’ intelligence. Same applies for nations who opt for economical socialism or the lack of anarchism. These protocols are just a sign of not intelligent enough individuals, or at least, not intelligent enough yet. And here is where hope resides.

I do not think this lack of intelligence is mainly lead by dumbness or psychopaths, but mainly by improvable traits such as ignorance and laziness.
