Wether economically or politically, I prefer protocols who better follow both of the 2 points mentioned. Because they better allow people to be the best version of themselves. They allow people to better leverage the natural biological mechanisms that have kept them alive and thriving for thousands of years in a more efficient, adaptive way.

And, if you allow me to intertwine sections, the only way to make dictatorships or oligarcracies sustainable would be by limiting human intelligence via limiting its natural exploration instinct. This seems impossible, every time you go against nature, at some point it explodes in your face in some way.

For example, drinking alcohol to keep you awake for the party and then the next day you can’t do much. For example, drinking coffee to work longer for a few days, you will end up with poor resting ability and higher levels of anxiety. For example, fighting a lion, you lose, and die.

Another way to delay the deadline of the unavoidable change, not to stop it, would be to keeping the population amount the same, or even reducing it. However, as long as knowledge is inherited, stored, and we do now self annihilate in a nuclear war, this will just be a slow down, as the natural human instinct of exploration will lead to the unavoidable ever growing complexity of wisdom.

Trying to sustain centralized and static power dynamics follows the same natural principle of something exploding in your face at some point. It is just that, due to the complexity of the situation, you need a certain combination of factors to align, which does not always happen, in order for the thing to explode in your face. But at some point, it will, by the natural forces already mentioned. And when that happens, the consequences can be as the ones described: from a hangover, to death, and extinction.

Even if we unrealistically assume that you manage to fully control the instinct to explore that all humans awaken and to keep population sizes equal, then your society will likely last less than if it was a more decentralized and dynamic one, because you will simply have a greater likelihood for this perfect storm of factors against you to appear.

8.2.2.2.- Why yes-es. More guns and more monkeys.

Often, lasting change comes from conviction and undeniable arguments in favor rather than reaction and arguments against “the alternative”. So let’s understand the conviction side of the matter.

Why oligarcracies or even dictatorships?

As said earlier, with oligarchies we can logically craft a complex scenario where a technocrat, because he is very intelligent, has control over some people and takes better decisions than the people he is controlling would take democratically.

We can say that it is safe to assume a technocrat as a very intelligent being due to having the capability of handling and developing technology, tools that solve problems, very complex ones usually.

In a very Cheerful way, a technocrat can say, as of X society, if we measure everyone’s intelligence we can actually see that we would operate better, in short or long term, if I rule. And he might be right.

Unfortunately, we can not measure this due to how complex and dynamic our society is and due to our limited measuring technologies. But the scenario showcased above is not illogical and it is plausible.

Dictatorships can also be argued in favor of via using a similar logic. For example, it can go as follows:

Some dictatorships might come from a period of a long civil war, under which a victorious side became a dictatorial regime. In this case, it can even be logically argued as this being good, in the sense of the lesser evil. Because under the fuzziness and chaos of a long lasting civil war, it can be deemed impossible to clearly convince everyone of who is the “bad one who deserves to lose”, therefore, before the impossibility of a rational end amidst chaos, the end of the chaos and beginning of any order is better than none.

And after the finalization of the war, it could be stated that the society was too fragmented internally to even function, and a firm tight grip is actually giving better results. And they might even be right in their claim, yet again, due to the complexity of modern human societies and the chaos of societies in conflict, we can not empirically confirm it by measuring with certainty all variables involved.

Our best approximation would be a historical analysis, which, obviously, is pure speculation based on texts which who know who actually wrote them and under which intentions and conditions. That is just not accurate enough for a convincing resolution that must coordinate all of people as in our current world.

From this we can see that the arguments in favor of less decentralized and dynamic protocols are based on logically correct but empirically impossible to verify claims.

Don’t be a fool either, arguments in favor of decentralized and dynamic protocols are the same. Yet, as I think they are the solution, I’m to lazy to focus on crafting them, but you can figure them out easily with similar reasons to the long ago mentioned one of someone who becomes drug addict when given freedom analysis. Something on the lines of:

How do you know, with empirical certainty, that, given freedom to someone, it will not use it to purposefully abuse others generating too much chaos or it will not just fall into some addiction?

Therefore they are, in practice, founded over a what-if belief applied on a single time-frame of a society. This analytical framework falls into the realm of what is usually known as social-sciences.

As we can not rigorously measure their origin and therefore conclude if they are needed we can though observe reality as is now and conclude, by deduction, that if our analysis of human nature is right, the fact that we are not yet, and we were not in the past, a species intelligent enough to form any other more decentralized and dynamic protocol that the ones we eventually had.

Furthermore, if you take this valid logical deduction and observe the current world you see a lack of democracies everywhere, in fact most of societies are oligarcracies. Therefore you can even conclude reasonably that we nowadays do need oligarcracies.

There will be endless arguments of the winners and losers of recent history, on, this happened because you did this thing at this specific time, others will say, that is a lie!, others will say, no, this other factor had more influence etc Some will say, you could have avoided this!, the one who could have avoided this will say, there was no choice because of this, this and that! Some will think they could have done it better if they would have been given a chance etc etc

All of them, and the humans that will listen to them, will remain though in their two-dimensional natural human analysis of good and evil.

In a scenario with so may possibilities our imagination can think of but none can be empirically verified by most of us. Reinforcing the need for ideologies and for groups of: I believe this is what it happened.

In some conflicts, the people who were actually there and know the truth, if the majority ends up believing a lie, will feel resentment or hopelessness, the people who thought there was an alternative will feel betrayed or hopeless again, the people who lost believing they are right will feel revengeful or… you guessed it hopeless.

And so on and so forth, without no one every truly knowing with certainty if the winners did all they could, and even without knowing, if the winners had the capability to do what they seemed to be able to do. The further in time the conflict lies, and the more complex it was, the harder it will be for making everyone agree on what actually happened, what could have been done, and what should have been done.

Whatever all those variables were, because of our incapability or reconstructing the sequence of events hat lead to the end result, we might reasonably conclude in a belief, a belief of, overall, we did needed that end and there was “no other choice” than that. Specially if that end result happened lots of times at historically close times all over the world. Like the formation of oligarcracies in the last century.

This is a fair argument, which leads to the conclusion I mentioned before of: we are not intelligent enough.

Yet, this argument can be broken. For that we must not be blinded by the past we will never see with certainty, we must find a solution based on a future we can walk towards with consistency.

Said in a less philosophical, less poetical way. We can break that argument with the old and always appearing human nature of exploration: One thing is who you are and what build and conditioned you in the past, and another completely different thing is who you can become. The impulse to explore, intellectually and physically, for the pursuit of a better life without the errors of the pats will always be a thing.

Do you really think humans are made to accept their current limitations and say for log periods of time: Yeah, we must be satisfied with oligarcracies ? They will be for some time, don’t be a fool, but the ever growing complexity of wisdom arisen from the vital need for exploration will eventually destroy you if you resist.

And here, the only way I can think of someone still being in favor of oligarcracies goes with the following argumentation. By the way, I won’t bother in arguing in favor of plutocracy as is obvious that money does not correlate with intelligence, the trait needed for optimal societal coordination. Anyway, the argument goes as follows:

Developing technology correlates with intelligence so, Charles, what you are mentioning here is the ideal case, but in practice it is clearly seen and known that the people in the masses are, on average, less intelligent than the all mighty engineers.

So, to some extent, in a society which is unavoidably hierarchical like human ones, isn’t it better to maximize the intelligence of the people in “higher” positions of the organizational ladder and hence put technocrats there? Therefore, shouldn’t we aim for a technocracy? An oligarcracy of technocrats where anyone can opt to gain power as long as it is a proven intelligent technocrat?

Even if I accept your argument of the ever growing complexity of wisdom, shouldn’t we walk towards there on technocratic steps?

The base idea is that a technocrat is more fit than any other person to rule, to organize the political institutions. Because he knows how to solve complex problems.

Well, the first argument that demolishes this idea is the following: That is just not enough, a problem as complex as societal coordination at scale, by the very same complexity and by the very same definition of the problem, requires managing lots of people. Technocrats might not be good at that. As solving complex technological problems does not always involve managing lots of people. For example a software engineer that can understand and write a complex code without talking to anyone else.

The counter argument in order to keep supporting technocracy would be: But wait, what about technocrat CEOs (the big boss) that worked on large companies? They not only are proven to be intelligent but also “good enough” at managing people while satisfying desires for a larger group.

The counter argument to the counter argument follows as:

Well, that is true as long as this technocrat was a boss or organizer on its previous position and it was working in a highly competitive market. Technocrats coming from monopolistic or oligopolistic markets are not fit. The ones coming from competitive markets know how to minimize abuse to their workers, because either they are empathetic or they must do it enforced by the market. If you abuse to much, workers have the possibility of leaving to the competing business. At the same time this profile of person also knows how to solve a complex technical problem, this one being creating a product the market demands.

If the market was not competitive we end up in a situation where a very intelligent and powerful individual can trick others into being abused without them realizing, worker exploitation. Which, in the political realm, the analogous phenomena he would produce is corruption. And as we saw, corruption is an abusive act, which we have to minimize in order to have societies that coordinate better, without too much chaos, unpredictability.

Argument: But okay, you said it yourself, let’s then create a technocracy where the leaders are the individuals with those specific traits: Boss of a large company in a competitive market.

Counter arguments:

1) How many of those people do exist in the world? These are juts very few people and we are just too many.

Furthermore, even assuming there are now currently enough. What about where they live? What about the future? Creating the oligarchic requirement for aspiring to control power of “only if you are this type of technocrat” creates also other physical problems.

Even if it was true that the profile of a technical ex-CEO of a large business in a competitive market is the best institution’s manager, that does not guarantee there will be one of them for every region or terrain a society lives in. Relying on its existence for the system to work is an unnecessary risk and we must not forbid anyone for reaching a political position because of that.

A dynamic system where we encourage paying more attention to the described figures as potential leaders might just work better than enforcing their participation creating a risk of shortages.

A democratic mechanism is just more adaptive and we should aim for it. A techno-democracy I might argue, where it works as a democracy but at a cultural level people tend to pay more attention to the described figures as potential leaders.

Still, even if this is culturally technocratic, we are talking about democratic rules of the game now.

2) Furthermore, even if there were enough, they have already chosen to not be politicians. How would we convert them? Will they change their minds and be more exposed as a figure of a public institution?

3) And most fundamentally: What incentives will there exist to assure the minimization of abuse once they are in power? Quick market dynamics providing feedback loops of information on what is wrong do no exist here, we are in the power realm now.

These people might just had been nice to employers due to the competitive market they were in, and as seen, power knows no to little competitors in other protocols other than democracy.

So nothing systematically assures you that an abuse minimization will be found if someone reaches power. We would eventually be relying on a small group of people’s desires which can easily go against the people they would be ruling, in this case, ruling over, not ruling for. And, this tends to chaos and more unpredictability over time due to the every growing complexity of wisdom.

The feedback loop of information processing in a democracy enables a more dynamic existence better aligned with human intrinsic behavior, the one who has made us survive so far.

A feedback loop of a democracy is the one which is as dynamic as possible given the unavoidable conditions of societal coordination at scale, in this case the organization of power dynamics, which mimics and re-creates the economical reason on why competition matters and makes products better, but in the realm of power.

It is true that in an oligarcracy there can still be elections, but these are limited to the voices vetted directly or more indirectly, by the oligarchs. Which reduces the amount of information you can extract from the feedback loops, as some real but ignored groups would be left out, making it less useful and therefore worsening the prediction capabilities or problem solving capabilities of the ruling group. Due to this core undeniable structural inefficiency on the feedback loop structure that oligarcracies have, democracy is just better for human well-being. Harder to properly implement, but if achieved, better.

Just like market dynamics in perfect competition but in the realm of power. In perfect competition, anyone who knows how to make a better product can access the mean to create it and, from the worker side, can freely move to work to competing businesses if they are being abused. In perfect competition of power, everyone who has a vision for its society can create a group to reflect it and show it to its neighbors. And if their neighbors are not satisfied with the current one or think the new one is better, they can just move towards it, faster or slower, but towards it.

The only thing that makes us solve problems are feedback loops, fix a variable and unfix it, an action with an associated reaction that carries error correcting information with it (learning), and in democracy, that feedback loops is just richer thanks to the possibility of more diverse reactions that allow us to better understand reality and then react accordingly as per our goals and interests.

The core natural principle in favor on richer feedback loop has already been presented long ago. In section 4.1.4.- What we now know, what we did, and the way forward to optimize power dynamics.

There we realized the unavoidable reality of large enough human societies where people start demanding simplified truths for complex problems due to biological cognitive limits mixed with the laziness in intelligence maximization. Which leads to the known phenomena of demagogy.

Concluding that chapter, the following sentences appeared:

“The goal for advancing our civilization is to change the rules of the game for power so they don’t depend that much on simplified truths.

All this follows logically from our intrinsic adaptation technique of the fixed variable resolution technique which is leveraged as seen in power dynamics. Mastering the understanding and use of it by improving the information management flow will generate the least friction possible in our coexistence.”

That argumentation still holds even more true today, as of when I’m writing this. I’m even more convinced of it after reading Robert Michels and realizing that, even in industrial times, societies still had the issue of the “stupid mass that can not comprehend”. However, in times where information accessing friction has been dramatically decreased, we have not yet found an improvement of the stupid mas. Signaling either that this effect will actually exist but takes one or two more generations to consolidate, or, signaling that there is something more fundamental in humans or our societal structures which makes the mass remain stupid.

It practice I think both are true, most of people don’t take as a core philosophy and goal for life the maximization of intelligence, and educational systems, as an example of pivotal societal structure, are made for the old times needs of learning capabilities. However, as we slowly or more quickly manage to get rid of this, I do think that the rules of the game for power and the technical application of them will depend way less of simplified truths.

In that section we saw how simplified truths will likely not lead us to correct solutions, specially in the modern world. Because they are ultimately guided by emotions, a biological tool coded for our tribal times, not the modern ones. A tool that will likely fail, one because the scenario now is more complex, and second because it is new and the solution, therefore, will also require some degree of novelty.

Not only this but as mentioned there too, simplified truths help nothing when controlling chaos:

“Artificial rivals deduced from a real intellectual effort to describe a problem, which might be true and real, but both of its simplified derived dichotomies are wrong to some extent as they have been created through a simplification of reality. And when simplifying you always miss little details that in complex systems tend to be crucial when trying to minimize chaos.

(...)

All these dichotomies, for learning purposes are not bad, but, for solving real life complex systems, they are. Those little details are as important as the whole. A small perturbation in the complex systems we live in can cause unpredicted, and probably undesired, consequences. Just like butterfly effects.”

Therefore, to shape a prosperous society in which we can figure out our best future possible and walk towards it, we should rely on as little simplified truths as possible.

Democracy, as per its richer feedback loop mechanism, allows the greatest minds to use their thinking more often and in more effective ways. The minds that apply the critical thinking and diminish the simplified truths phenomena.

Whereas in more centralized and static protocols, these minds are likely silenced and can not efficiently execute the act of critical thinking. Increasing the amount of simplified truths with all the known risks we have observed from them, like poorer feedback loops.

But, and big but, all this is true as long as your entity is capable of processing the information without overheating.

As said on the economics part, sometimes we do need this simpler models to exist because we can not manage to create nor understand collectively the functioning of more complex ones. But that should not make us ignore or deny the superiority of the more complex ones. We must acknowledge our starting point, think like an engineer, figure out improvements, and work towards them.

I can only keep thinking of more staticness-risks that a technocracy brings with it. So, again, even if it is realistic and logical for certain kinds of technocrats to perform better, we should not just systematically await for them to appear in a big enough amount and after that, to wait and pray so their desires are aligned with ours, for the functioning of our societies. We should aim for the system on its own to reflect the trends of a functioning thriving and lasting society. So in practice we do not improve at the pace of exceptions, but at the pace of us just existing, regardless of exceptions and even benefiting more from them when they occur, as they will have a voice so everyone takes them into account.

We can keep cycling the argumentation in favor of oligarcracies by recycling on and on with different wording the “gun-to-monkey” principle:

Argument: But opening the gate to non-technocrats creates the risk of someone really bad at managing getting the role.

Counter-argument: That is true, but you will never delete that. Freedom is the ability to explore, and exploring brings risk with it, always. The only way to make sure the negative side of the risk does not appear or it appears as less as possible is with responsibility. The ability to recognize the failure points and taking charge of them.

And democratic systems, as they align representatives with represented, create responsibility. Minimizing always this risk.

Furthermore, because they have a richer feedback loop than oligarcracies, the information and detection of this risk is improved. Assuming the individuals represented are intelligent enough to handle it. Which is a logical assumption in a society that is successfully managing a complex democratic protocol.

Yet only technocracies, do not minimize any inherent risk, in fact they have the inherent risk of not existing enough profile-matching-technocrats. They are systematically more fragile while democracy is systematically designed to be risk minimized. And I’m not even mentioning the annihilating argument which I’m tired of mentioning already: the every growing complexity of human wisdom.

Facing the risk of a bad leader through revocable representation of anyone is more effective than facing the risks of gate-closing the system to a select few.

Furthermore, thanks to this, democracy also opens the door for other types of specialist to appear, those specialized on the management of their region. And these masters can learn from the technocrats, while at the same time the technocrats can just mind their own business, literally, ruling their own business way better.

This is the already known benefit that the idea of specialization in the production process brings. Technocracies give technocrats the responsibility of also managing and having to worry about power and the nuances of regions, giving way more variables to them and increasing the likelihood of poor performance or failure.

Democracy is better because these power and region specific specialists can be created with the temporary technocrat help with organizational techniques teaching and then each one follows its own path more efficiently. The principle of revocability allows the technocrats to delegate to the masses that role. Now it is up to the masses to do it right.

If a technocrat does not support it then it just means that he does not trust the masses. Like not giving an employee a role because you don’t trust it will do it right. The “gun-to-monkey” principle.

But again, if the masses show a clear understanding of democracy and how to implement and manage it, then democracy is superior too due to this separation of concerns mechanic that it enables. And due to all the so many times mentioned other benefits of dynamism and decentralization for human problem solving.

We could be going, on and on, thinking about arguments and counter arguments, crafting specific examples of scenarios where democracy is superior, and where certain kinds of oligarcracies are superior too. As we saw at the very beginning, everything is just statistics, and almost anything is theoretically possible to happen at some point in time.

As you might have seen, the only way to attack democracy is by destroying one of its pillars, what if people vote something that was actually wrong, like not being able to discern a valid leader/organizer? But the same critique can be made to oligarchic systems with voting. And here we go again, what if we give a gun to a monkey? What if we bite more than we can chew?

Quite an useless critique because we are ultimately saying: what if X is capable of Y but X happens not to be capable of Y in a percentage of the time, and that time arrives? Theoretically logical critique, yet useless for any informed action. As it carries no information because it is always true for any X and Y.

Human existence is way bigger than politics or economics, if we aim to systematically improve it, we must aim to understand all vital sections of it, and education and intelligence are a crucial part too.

Do we need oligarchies as per the current state of the world? Seems like it. Should we accept this and that is it?  Clearly not, we are made to keep refining our systems or as we have seen, a perfect storm will come and we will become extinguished. The next step is clear, democracy… Or is it? More on the following sections.

To start wrapping this up, supporting a technocracy, after all these arguments, can only be done by follows similar reasons on wether to make drug consumption illegal or to just educate and make people very aware of its bad consequences.

Everyone knows the second way makes sense, but still some oppose it because they do not trust themselves or their neighbors’ capability of executing it. Again, and for the last time, the gun-to-monkey principle.

Everyone knows democracy makes more sense than technocracy but the ones who defend technocracy do not trust themselves or others into properly creating and handling a democracy. At a national level, given education and deep thought, not choosing democracy is fundamentally based on trust issues.

These are solved by education, learning, defeating intellectual laziness, listening and communicating calmly to foster trust.

At international levels, due to the absence of a Wolrd Government, in scenarios of crisis, not having a democracy might arise too from a stronger foreign nation influencing yours in such a chaotic way that create those trust issues in order to better control you as more centralized and static systems are better to control. But not because your society is not ready for a democracy, but because it is being abused by another, or other, nations, consciously or unconsciously at both parts of the abusive pair.

Again, the other nation that would be abusing yours might be doing it, a analyzed, by 2 reasons, lack of intelligence of figuring out better ways of interacting with you, or, thinking it is capable of controlling you without generating too much chaos it can not control.
Regardless of the motivations for the abuse, at some point, if you want your society to be more decentralized and dynamic the solution of education, learning etc etc will be required. Once that is done, there are multiple ways to handle the relation with the abusive nation or nations, but that will be discussed in a later section.
Concluding, even if today we need oligarcracies because we can not manage to peacefully transition to democracies, I aim for democracy. Because it is in the human nature to learn, teach, explore and keep refining the processes that make this life more enjoyable.

X.- Conclusion 8.2.1

For all these reasons explained through the 8.2.2 sections, I aim for democracy, for now. Notice I did not say choose, I said aim for. It depends on the context.

In our current context, I do not think democracies are possible, but, precisely because of that I’m putting my life’s effort in improving everyone’s education on how to maximize their intelligence and gather useful knowledge so they do become capable of a peaceful transition into creating, managing and maintaining democratic systems.

As with the economics part: I do not think we should aim for plutocracies or technocracies, or any kind of oligarcracy, or dictatorship. But, current world observations as the lack of libertarian economies and the lack of democracies in the world seem to indicate the centralized and static models are the only viable solutions for now.

So, again, I aim for democracy, and probably, I aim for anarchism too, yet in the far future, one where we can actually realistically think about it. A pity that by then I will have likely died by natural causes.

8.2.1.- On how to create a democratic system. A glimpse into the complexity.

Here I will give my best attempt to explain a democratic design and showcase technical ideas to actually implement it. I’m currently working on creating a constitution that is usable in any society that aims to be democratic based on these principle and more. At the end of the day, the design of checks and balances a democracy requires is very aligned to the hacker’s mindset I’ve developed and to the nature of the systems I’m specialized in: CDNs (Consensus based Database Networks), most popularly know nowadays as blockchain or cryptocurrencies.

All I learned about from the other realm of knowledge that political science is was created by Antonio García Trevijano, another Spanish human, rest in peace.

Trevijano wrote all his thoughts on what actually is democracy and how to create it, in general but also showcasing the specific Spanish case on his book: Teoría Pura De La República Constitucional.

It is a hard to read book because it uses old and complex words and it has lots of references to other philosophers’ concepts, historical facts etc And as far as I know it is only in Spanish. Fortunately enough we got AI. If you want to read it just copy-paste pages of the book and translate it to english.

This being said, we can understand as democracy a political regime characterized by its decentralization and dynamism.

That it is achieved via allowing small amounts of people to create new power aspirants and via separating the capabilities of the State into three different independent entities.

The decentralization and dynamism is created in the hope that it will lead to lower degrees of abuse and greater degrees of adaptation.

As per decentralized and dynamic systems, their design and inner workings are more complex than other more centralized or static systems.

Due to their natural by design complexity, the creation of such a system can only be achieved with higher amounts of intelligence than other simpler systems.

On top of that, if the democratic system is wrongly designed, by natural forces as explained, will tend to collapse or risks collapsing in more centralized and static regimes.

Thus, due to their complexity and their nature, stable lasting democracies require more intelligent individuals for their conception and maintenance.

So, a democracy, if we do not care about how much it lasts, is defined by:

- Existence of a State, a body that holds the monopoly on violence.

- Separation and independence from one another of the different capabilities of a State: to think (legislative), to act (executive), to observe and reason (judicial).

- Capability of a small amount of citizens to create their own completely independent power aspiring alternative.

- Capability for most of the citizens to do the previous creation act and to participate on the elections of the State.

Now, due to the sheer size of our societies, we need representatives. So, in practice, democracies in our societies need one more trait in their definition:

- Authentic representation through single-member elections in small electoral districts. Having the represented body the capability of firing the representative anytime.

In smaller societies, like the classical Athens from hundreds of years ago, there was no need for this last trait. People could vote directly, at least the ones who were allowed to do so. Simplified they were the adults, non-slave males with citizenship.

Anyway, the need for representatives creates a new relation of power between entities on the system: representative, represented.

As seen, any power relation can lead to abuse, so we must minimize it. And as seen too, decentralization and dynamism tend to work well given intelligent individuals.

So, via breaking down large societies in small electoral districts, we decentralize the solution. This helps as, in a small district, the power representative will see on the streets the represented ones, and thus, if something is abused, it can have real implications on his live with his neighbors. Real action, real reaction.

From the previous paragraph we can deduce that the represented must have lived and will live in the electoral district for some time as a requisite for the decentralization benefits to manifest.

The dynamism is added by the revocation capability. If the representative, at any time, can be taken away by the represented body, in case of abuse, it will be over soon. This dynamism allows for better adaptive tendencies and creates a natural break, a natural antagonistic force to the power which is temporarily delegated to the representative from the represented one. This helps the system re-balance and not to have an inertia towards centralization and static behavior.

The relation we have analyzed now is just 1 power relation pair in a democratic system. The representative-represented pair. But it is way more complex, there are more pairs to analyze:

- Executive, judicial.
- Executive, legislative.
- Executive, citizens.
- Judicial, legislative.
- Judicial, citizens.
- Legislative, citizens.
- Representatives, legislative.

All these pairs require intelligent design so to create a decentralized and dynamic system with good incentives that lead to minimal or no abuse.

All this is what Trevijano explores on his book while proposing real solutions to balance everything.

I do think that the concepts and technical details explained on that book should be understood by any human in the world.

Not only because, as explained, I aim for democracy, but because the only way for people to create a democracy is for them to know what a democracy truly is.

A lasting democracy, as explained, can only be created by intelligent enough people coordinating. Trevijano called this requirement: proceso de libertad constituyente (process of constituent freedom).

A process in which the great majority of a society is given freedom to chose and propose any possible future and, if chosen a democratic one, truly transition to a that regime.

The process has more details than that, I’m just explaining the overall ideas.

Trevijano explores lots of economical and political self-balancing structures to assure no abuse, or minimal abuse of power. And to assure that if it ever happens, it can be punished.

Some of the following only make sense assuming an intelligent knowledgeable population, the one a lasting democracy requires for its mere conception.

A non-exhaustive list of them are:

- Any political group can not receive any kind of private donation or public funding. It must only be funded by fixed quotas of their members.

- In electoral campaign, public advertisement will be illegal. Known public venues, like schools, will be the only places where political campaign acts will be possible. Each candidate must have the same amount of space and time to speak in each public venue.

- If the country becomes inoperable due to the legislative and executive powers clashing. They can destruct each other at the cost of destructing themselves and creating new elections for both.

- There can be no judge that is chosen by any other part of the other two State powers.

- The districts must be no bigger than 100.000 people.

- There must be separate elections for the executive and the legislative power.

- If someone is chosen in 1 of the branches of power of the State, he can not be in any other in the current mandate nor in the next one.

- If someone power holding person abuses power, that person is immediately kicked out and can not hold any kind of public role for X years (let’s say 15).

The book is really interesting, and the reasons on why these technicalities work independently and together to create a real democracy, in the sense that is real because it will last, are even more interesting too.

Please read it, it will take time and it is a hard read, but it is worth it. On the meanwhile, I’m working myself in the previously mentioned general constitution book that builds on top of Trevijano’s work and aims to even improve it and refine it.

X.- Conclusion: Section 8.2.

This is why I aim for democracy and this is what I mean by democracy. Remember, if you are reading this from a non-democratic country, like mine, as a general rule, do not rush too much.

I recommend not to panic. We have been working as oligarchracies or even dictatorships and we are not extinguished yet. Do not guide yourself by what you see on social media, it is all exaggerated, guide yourself by what you hear when talking and listening to your neighbors or real people in real time.

Getting there requires communication, education, thinking etc Mainly energy demanding cognitive actions. It takes time and effort. Specially more if the current power regime fights against it. A great effort with minimized chaos is required.

Remember, reject chaos. Chaotic protest are more likely to fail because they signal bad organization, and a bad organization won’t create any revolution towards the existing ones, specially if they have been there for a while already.

I understand that unfair situations awaken emotions and can lead to chaos. I’m just trying to friendly remind that that is not the best way and we should aim to master our rational selves to pull out the most intelligent and harder to carry out outcome.

Luckily there are ways so to the current powers fight less against a revolution or directly do not fight and even support it.

It is not easy at all, it can be impossible in some cases, but by all being Cheerful, power holding people and citizens, we can make it as real as it can actually be.

The goal is not to dethrone people and put new ones, the goal is not to get richer, the goal is to make everyone more intelligent so we can coordinate better and achieve greater and more lasting happiness via the creation and maintenance of every time more decentralized and dynamic protocols.

You can make that inside any power regime, with patience just by being a selfless teacher, educate people, yourself, try make them respectfully grow. And slowly and organically democracy should come.

This advise comes from what I am observing in my country. In Spain we had a dictatorship long ago, 1939-1978. When the dictator died then we transitioned to an oligarcracy, yet due to: reasons, the people were brainwashed into thinking it is a democracy. The thing is that this transition was peaceful, because it was not a drastic change.

The transition to a more decentralized system did not come fully from within, external nations, with more decentralized and dynamic power mechanics, influenced with economical pressure for example, on Spain’s “democratic” transition.

Despite this, I think with an intelligent enough population, like a Cheerful population, a nation can still transition to a more decentralized and dynamic system without the need of international interests influencing.

The thing is that now, slowly but surely, lots of people are realizing that Spain is not a democracy and why exactly that is. Knowledgeable people have been explaining why for decades, Trevijano himself was alive and on exile when the dictatorship and did not stop preaching that Spain was an oligarcracy and not a democracy until he died.

As a curious observation, maybe, if we do not want more wars, we might have to pass through a period of oligarcracies when coming from dictatorships in order to transition to democracies. It makes sense, as this transition is smoother and less prone to trauma and tension. 

In Spain, agnostic to public money, associations of citizens are peacefully preaching how we should change the entire political system, from its deepest roots, the constitution and all, to make it a true democracy.

It truly seems like, we can transition to decentralized and dynamic systems without the need for wars. We just have to be patient selfless teachers.

That is what I meant with no rush, big changes require drastically different actions, which, if you are not intelligent enough, they can easily lead to uncontrolled chaos that does more bad than good.

I do not recommend drastic actions, but I get that, if survival is not granted, they are not an option but just an impulse, an instinct.

I know that some oppressive regimes will have killed families and other horrendous stuff. Repeating myself, when survival is not granted, Cheerfulism requires a miracle to be triggered.

I wish the best of lucks to the most extreme circumstances. Yet please do not forget, at the end of the day, we should land in a place where the idea of “the other” does not exist. Where the thing that exists is “another me” or “my neighbor”. At personal levels and international levels.

8.3.- The best way forward I can think of: CDL.

Finally, after explaining all these details, I can propose the way forward for all societies.

So, by being Cheerful, by living abiding as much as I could by the human axioms, here is what I concluded to be the best way we can manage to exist as a society. Feel free to frame it from another angle of reality, I would love to read that.

The answer is CDL. Which stands for:

Cheerfulism, Democracy and Libertarianism.

I think the members of this triad balance each other beautifully. I will dare to say perfectly.

There is a deep trait that is always present in effective solutions that we humans have thought of. We saw this in the power dynamics coordination problem, the resource management problem and the educational problem. The common trait is:

Decentralizing variable handling, a.k.a. problem solving, to proven intelligent individuals.

The 3 components of CDL strongly aligns a society to this principle in some way or another.

Let’s understand why CDL works well by understanding the individual weaknesses of its parts.

Democracy’s failure is: What the majority decides might just not be a good decision. The same way individuals can take bad decisions, societies can too in a democracy.

Libertarianism’s failure is: A free human does not really exist and therefore it can still abuse others and take bad decisions.

So just by these 2 protocols we are still not optimizing for the minimization of abuse or optimization of happiness.

For precisely that we need Cheerfulism. Cheerful individuals are less likely to take bad decisions due to their focus on maximizing intelligence. Furthermore it naturally leads to less abuse. This is because intelligent individuals realize that they must live with others, and they can also realize that cooperation over competition or conflict is a less chaotic, easier to manage, solution on the long term.

Sure, if they are too dumb, they can just not be capable of realizing this and abuse will occur. There is always that theoretical and statistical risk. Personally, as per personal experience, most people do realize that cooperation is better than conflict in the long term. Otherwise frequent street fights would be normalized in all around the globe. Yet there is a big chunk of it where frequent normalized street fights do not happen. Signaling that this is just ignorance leading to poor coordination. Or other controllable abuse sources instead of uncontrollable ones like dumbness or psychopathy.

If uncontrollable sources of abuse were the main cause of violence on the world then violence would exist everywhere, it would be the norm in each street. But it does not, so it can be controlled to some extent, thereby we should maximize for that.

Another negative point for democracy and libertarianism is that they are harder to implement because they require more complex systems created and maintained by a higher collective intelligence. Cheerfulism also balances that by promoting the maximization of each person’s intellectual capabilities.

Continuing, libertarianism and democracy are the most capable protocols for allowing the decentralization of variable handling to intelligent individuals, which tends to better outcomes. Each in their respective fields or problems, these are economy and politics.

But, as another missing trait of these two protocols, none says anything about how to create intelligent individuals. Cheerfulism does.

Let’s keep naming weak spots. Democracy and libertarianism guide people with the goal and premise of a future with more freedom. But freedom was never the desire at the deepest core of human nature.

More fragile becomes the soul of a group without a goal that is really shared and biological, that is what Cheerfulism is for too. To guide ourselves towards a goal we will always share, the goal of happiness.

Nonetheless, I want to clarify that it is not one or the other, it is which one should we prioritize and use as the main guidance.

I think a better engine, a better core principle that leads to more human well-being can be reached if we focus mainly on happiness and not on freedom, because it is more natural and its search is always real, all the time, regardless.

Sure, only after survival is granted. But freedom operates in the same way, no-one seeks freedom when they starve, they seek food. I’m assuming granted survival as said earlier.

People gather and party together, they bond together, because they are ultimately feeling happy, not because they are feeling free. Freedom can make you feel happy, and that is why we ultimately like it and can get addicted to it. Not vice-versa.

Any source of happiness brings the risk of addiction with it. Some are easier to fall into, some are harder, but all do bring the risk. This is another reason why we must not ignore the intelligence part.

Regardless of freedom seekers or protection seekers, if you seek happiness, you can talk to both and they will not perceive you as the other, because you have common ground. Because happiness is a deeper shared truth, it can help us coordinate with less conflict too.

As a metaphor for this. Libertarianism and socialism are a couple that broke up due to misunderstandings and lack of communication lead arguments. Cheerfulism would be the common friend who still hangs out with both, which is listened by and listens to both, and has the capability of fixing the relationship in the future.

When we guide ourselves based on deeper principles that always hold, we can reach deeper understandings and reach greater goals by crafting more effective and complex solutions. And for successful guidance, regardless of what is the core you choose, regardless of freedom or happiness, you have to mix it with the maximization of intelligence for optimal well-being and being able to handle chaos and uncertainty, which conform risk. Cheerfulism is both, happiness and intelligence.

Ultimately I’m not libertarian and seek to maximize freedom, I’m Cheerful and I seek to maximize intelligence and optimize happiness, I can only think and reason through deeper principles when I think of happiness, and that, overall, leads to more understanding that has greater potential of prosperity.

As a scientific parallelism, some Einstein equations can be “simplified” logically and correctly into Newton’s ones. This doe not mean Newton is always wrong, the same way in which putting individual freedom at the core is not always wrong, it just means that Einstein’s equations hold true for a larger set of reality’s contexts. Happiness focus would be Einstein, Newton would be freedom focus. However, you need to be intelligent to discover and use any of them.

Concluding with my favoritism to Cheerfulism, because action (power) and means (resources) are nothing without a deeply shared goal (happiness). And because failure awaits us in the future if we do not think and adapt (intelligence).

These are the reasons why we need to add Cheerfulism to this triad.

A triangle shaped engine of action, representing the self-balancing principle it leads to: CDL.

But hey, let’s not rush, we still have to talk about the weakness of Cheerfulism. It has an unavoidable flaw: We can still make mistakes, we can still take bad decisions.

That is why I always repeat, it is all statistics, we can not assure success, just optimize for its likelihood to be greater. That is what CDL aims for.

Also, if resources are truly limited, then survival instincts kick-in, critical thinking gets kicked-off and Cheerfulism is turned-off.

That is why, even if there is a fight for survival-related resources, we must not forget, that after the fight, CDL is what we must strive to achieve.

8.3.1.- How to transition to CDL.

There are 7 possible combinations of current societies as per if they follow CDL or not.

These are the 3 different variables:

- Cheerful or not Cheerful.
- Democratic or not democratic.
- Libertarian or not libertarian.

All possible starting points are:

1.- Cheerful, Not-Democratic, Libertarian.
2.- Cheerful, Democratic, Not-Libertarian.
3.- Cheerful, Not-Democratic, Not-Libertarian.
4.- Not-Cheerful, Democratic, Libertarian.
5.- Not-Cheerful, Not-Democratic, Libertarian.
6.- Not-Cheerful, Democratic, Not-Libertarian.
7.- Not-Cheerful, Not-Democratic, Not-Libertarian.

The ideal transitions are the ones the image that follows shows.

In red you will see the harder to change states and harder to change transitions, in yellow, less hard to change ones, and in green, the easiest ones and the end goal:



I think these are the best paths to follow, and now I will explain why.

I think the best first step is for a society to become Cheerful. Because Cheerful individuals adapt better, which will only facilitate the other possible transition steps.

You can see that the process requires at most 3 steps and, as little, 1 step. The goal is to all states, all circles, to follow these arrows and reach the green state: CDL.

Furthermore, as per their intelligence and happiness oriented action, Cheerful individuals do not like chaos and tend not to create it, as it is harder to control and live through. If it is unavoidable or mistakes are taken as per human nature, chaos will arise or be chosen though.

Even in that case, in the case of conflict, they are the best enemies you can have. As their traits naturally lead them to minimize abuse, thus revenge is less likely or less severe.

After a Cheerful transition, then I think the best next step is a democratic transition. This is a complex topic that will be addressed later in the chapter.

Wether you come from oligarchic power dynamics or dictatorial ones, it is likely that powerful individuals will have abused their power. So transitioning to a system where they have less can be scary to them. How to deal with it was covered in chapter 4. In part, as mentioned there, a transition through education is the safest bet for abusive powerful-ones. Thus this is another reason why understanding the system of education, chapter 6, is so vital.

The reasons on why aiming for transitioning to a democracy where explained in chapter 4 and 7.2.

And finally, the last step, a transition to libertarianism.

I do not think libertarianism is possible under non-democratic regimes. At least not for more than short time periods. This is because oligarchies and small groups of individuals can always be bribed every now and then by wealthy enough individuals or groups. Bribery is an act that can lead to abuse. Abuse creates chaos and that makes intelligent adaptation more difficult.

A non-democratic and libertarian system would be one where money moves very freely and power does too, which, by natural inertia in similar ways of those explained in previous sections, those two forces, instead of clashing against each other, will just tend to go in the same direction because it is easier: centralization, static behavior, thus lack of adaptation, and eventually abuse. Sure, exceptions can happen, but exceptions are.

The reasons on why aiming for transitioning to libertarianism were explained in chapter 5.

And as seen, changes, of any kind, are better done and handled through education. Specially education aligned with human nature. For that refer to all explained in chapter 6.

Note that the graph presented is incomplete, of course a country can go from state 7 to state 5 for example. For simplicity, I’ve just drawn and explained the ones which I think are the best transitions.

I could draw all transitions from all states and argue against why those are not the best, but that would be a total of 28 transitions to analyze. I will leverage my laziness and encourage you to train your engineer’s thinking by analyzing them.

For example, the one mentioned from state 7 to state 5. I think it is less optimal because it would naturally would go back to state 7. For the reason explained above, a libertarian not-democratic regime does not last long. Thus it would go back to state 7: non-libertarian, non-democratic.

We could further complete the graph with diversifying the not-something tags. Like instead of not-democratic, specifying: dictatorship or oligarchic. Instead of not-libertarian specifying: socialist, communist, anarchist. Instead of Cheerful: any other predominant philosophy.

If we do this, we would have a graph where every single society on earth would belong to one of its nodes. And then, each person, according to their situation would just have to optimize the path to reach the green CDL node.

An advice that arose from personal observation. If your country is a dictatorship, it is harder to transition directly to a democracy, it might be less chaotic to first transition to an oligarchy and then to a democracy. If you want to do drastic changes then you must make sure all your society is intelligent enough, otherwise you will get chaos and either not create a transition or even move in the opposite direction.

I hope all of you think about this, on your society, and where it fits on the graph and what is the optimal path to reach the CDL. I’ve done it for mine.

8.3.2.- A factor is missing in the name: Education.

CDL is missing an E. Which stands for EBTAA, the already mentioned in earlier chapters, Education Based on Trust Accountability and Adaptation.

In any kind of transition from a non-CDL state to a more aligned CDL state, you nee change, and the key of effective and efficient change, as seen is learning, educating.

Wether in the transition from non-libertarian to libertarian, from non-Cheerful to Cheerful, or from non-democratic to democratic, an effective and efficient education is vital.

Specially in the power dynamics part of the triad, as explained in the world peace chapter, abuse can not be deleted, just minimize, the education of future generations plays a crucial role in the most optimal and realistic technique for transitioning from one power protocol that likely had abuse to another one where power is more decentralized. This was the technique of temporary clearly pretended ignorance.

And as explained in the education chapter and as highlighted on chapter, humanity is facing a challenge which is that most of people are too lazy to train their brains. This has similar barriers than the ones people have to not start physical training. And, the best way to create a habit, which is what training ultimately is, is to teach it during the early years of a human.

When people get older, change, training, gets harder, thus getting used to it at early stages in life is essential.

So, even if education, and specially EBTAA is not in the name. It is inside CDL. CDL can only be possible when people have trained their brains. Which is easily achieved if starting in early stages of life, done properly through an EBTAA based education.

8.3.3.- The international factor influence on the transition.

All said it is fine in a national context, however in international landscapes, this ideal transition paths presented might not be possible.

Because some nations depend on abusing others, therefore, they will likely not help, in fact they might even put impediments towards other nations that are being abused so to transition either to Cheerfulism, democracies or libertarian protocols, because if they succeed on the mission, those abused nations will be way harder to abuse. And the abusive nation will lose all the good it was getting from the abuse.

As seen in the abuse section, abusers might abuse because of 2 reasons: lack of intelligence due to stupidity or dumbness which leads to them unable to figure out better less abusive or maybe even non-abusive ways of interacting with you, or, because of he abuser thinking he is capable of controlling you without generating uncontrollable chaos on the process.

This matter is a complex one. Because the factors that affect the eventual action of a nation abusing another are very varied. For example, a nation might accidentally abuse another one because they vote a government that has a very aggressive international attitude, however maybe the voters did not intend that and they are not capable of realizing it because they are focused on other matters which are perceived with a higher priority than international actions.

The abusive action might not even have a voting mechanism and the decision is dependent on a small group of oligarchs which might overestimate their capabilities of abuse etc.

Regardless of the configuration and the entity who decides to abuse, the fundamental drivers of the abuse are the 2 reasons explained.

I could get theoretical again and analyze every combinations. But that would take likely triplicating the length of this book, in my opinion, unnecessarily.

As per my current understanding, I think most of the international abuse happens is driven with the strongest force by the scenario of people being to cognitively busy with other topics rather than international dilemmas.

I’m talking specially a very specific nation which is clearly starting to see and feel the limits of biting more than it can chew, trying to control by force and corruption others. However, as said, names do not matter, what matter is understanding.

I’m aware that in the international landscape some nations won’t be able to transition ideally to CDL, even if they so desire, due to external abuse. However, if the abuser transitions to CDL, the abuse applied externally will be reduced, as more intelligent individuals will be able to solve their current tensions better.

And in scenarios of less tension, arises trust and clarity, which further promotes finding middle ground of agreement that reduces abuse.

These chains of thought resemble a lot the ones in the world peace chapter. Because they are based on the same realistic fundamental dynamics.

So, as with world peace, if we want our society to move towards CDL we can not just logically wait for it to happen, we must strive for it. And if we all strive for it at the same time, mutual understanding will be maximized.

8.3.2.- CDL applied to Spain.

How could it be otherwise, because I’m Spanish and I know this society better than any other, here I will showcase an example of a manifesto for the Spanish population on how I think  they should transition to CDL.

For context, Spain is economically socialist and politically an oligarcracy. Philosophically, to be honest, I do not really know. People do not seem to have a main train of thought, as modern artists say, this is the remix.

We do actually have strong christian religious values roots and influence though, even though its practice has weakened a lot, philosophy wise we are sort of aligned with that.

Anyway, unless a religion or predominant philosophy is strongly opposed of making people more intelligent, which does not seem to be the case on Spanish one, transitioning to Cheerfulism should just be compatible with any other predominant philosophy or religion.

A very strong feature of Cheerfulism is that, because it is so aligned with human nature, it does not really matter with which other religion or philosophy has to coexist with. Cheerfulism does not deny, negate or censor their existence, it just supports them and dances along with them. Just as the image at the beginning of the chapter.

This same reasoning also applies to economical, political or educational adaptations.

Given this context on Spain and the viability analysis of Cheerfulism on it, this could be some action principles based on CDL for Spain:

CDL - Spain
(Cheerfulism, Democracy and Libertarianism)

1.
Spain should adopt Cheerfulism as a guiding philosophy.

2.
Spain should transition to a true democracy.
CDL defines democracy as the system that adheres to the three principles established by Antonio García-Trevijano on his work "Teoría Pura de la República":

- Separation of the three powers of government at their origin.

- Authentic representation through single-member elections in small electoral districts.

- Collective political freedom as the foundation of the system.

3.
Spain should move toward a strongly libertarian economic system.
CDL defines libertarianism as the next step of centralization beyond anarchism. In a libertarian society, public money exists but is kept to the minimum necessary to fund a public army that enforces the law. Individuals have private money and may use it freely to organize resources, as long as they do not break the law.

4.
Every point described here is a recommendation. CDL does not impose change, it recommends it, specially via education. It believes that the most prosperous change comes from conviction, not coercion.

5.
Spain’s education should be based on the principles of EBTAA: Education based on trust, accountability and adaptation.

6.
The points above are based on logical reasoning inferred from human biology: a human being
always strives to be happy, and to succeed in that task it is essential to cooperate intelligently with one's neighbors.

Cooperation requires a balance of power that prevents, as much as physically possible, one
neighbor from abusing another. Therefore, a democratic system is recommended. The imperfection of democracy is summed up by the phrase: “If the people are foolish, foolish things will be decided.” Hence, CDL also promotes the philosophy of Cheerfulism as a counterbalance to this weakness.

To understand happiness and to maximize human intelligence, one must understand the
Cheerfulist philosophy.

And for the most efficient allocation of resources, it is recommended to combine this with an
economic system that strongly tends toward libertarianism. It must be emphasized that this system is not perfect, and just as the branches of power check and balance one another in a democracy, the inefficiencies and contradictions of libertarianism are counterbalanced by democracy and by the Cheerful citizens. Thus, CDL aims to coordinate the three fundamental pillars of any society. In this case, the Spanish society: mind (processing and analysis of information), force (the body’s action), and organization (coordination of information into action).

All this transition catalyzed by the usage of an EBTAA educational system and attitude. One that promotes a revenge minimized transition and habits to maintain the effort required to order the existing and potential chaos.

6.
CDL recommends these principles of action to every known human society, adapting the transition process described in point 7 to the social reality in each case.

7.
In the Spanish case, CDL recommends the following transition from the current system to the
proposed one:

- First: Emphasize Cheerfulism, to clarify the goals and principles of action. At the same time, introduce to the people the understanding of EBTAA.

- Second: Emphasize achieving real democracy, so that Cheerful individuals may begin to act using their fullest potential and power decentralization is carried out with minimal cycles of hate.

- Last: Emphasize the pros and cons of the libertarian economic model, so that, in a democratic system with a Cheerful mindset, its implementation may begin.

- The transition is recommended to be as peaceful as possible through temporary clearly pretended ignorance towards the disastrous acts of the current oligarchies. These are the political class and any individual which its monetary income depends fully on the State and the wasting or inefficient spending of public funds.

Hatred leads to chaos, and in chaos, prosperity is hindered. However, violence is sometimes inevitable by nature, and punishment of the clearly abusive faction of the oligarchy will occur if society so demands.

Still, CDL strongly recommends avoiding such punishment, although it will not actively work to stop it if it unfolds.

In the case of a transition from the Spanish Oligarchic system to a democratic one, the usage of temporary clearly pretended ignorance (TCPA) would make sense.

As per Trevijano’s analysis, since real democracy can only arise from absolute social conviction and action, TCPA is doable in a democratic transition because the same strong conviction and action is required for succesfully executing TCPA. 

However, due to Spain’s population size, as TCPA only minimizes revenge, any famous oligarch related to known corruption cases is at risk of a minority hunting him or her. Maybe even at risks of being killed because of their accumulated negligence cases through the decades which have actually caused real deaths. Like in the recent 2024 DANA floodings in Valencia’s territory.

Due to Spain’s great levels of debt, spending more money on the protection of these individuals is discouraged and exile is the cheapest option. Either way, the oligarchs holding fame related to negligence or corruption must be either protected or exiled to abide by TCPA and create the less chaos possible.

8.
CDL has no leader.

Although it was created by Spanish citizen Carlos Alegre Urquizú, CDL is a set of ideas intended to transform Spanish society by winning what is popularly known as the cultural battle. Thus, the figure of the creator holds no power over the ideas once they are explained.

As long as a person defends these eight points, they may consider themselves part of CDL, regardless of any other factor.

Any political or other organization created to promote CDL’s principles must clearly state that it is not CDL. For example, if the creator were to found a political party, its name should reflect that it is a personification of the ideas, not the ideas themselves: e.g. CDL-PP (Cheerfulness, Democracy, Liberty – Political Party).

If that party ultimately fails to adhere to these principles, CDL will remain unaffected, as it is a set of ideas and not a physical being nor collective.

This distinction is intended to help citizens foster critical thinking and debate about ideas themselves, rather than about the people trying to apply them. In this way, society is encouraged to focus on goals and clear methods to achieve them, and thus they are less likely to elevate any leader or leaders into a fanaticism based tyranny.

X.- Conclusion: Chapter 8.

This chapter marks the end of part 2 of the book. Here I’ve connected, polished and summarized all the ideas and analysis on what I think it can happen if we manage to become Cheerful.

The rest is up to you.

Will you be willing to train your mind? Will you be willing to understand happiness and realize what patterns bring it to you?

Will you be able to combine both in order to figure out ways to get them in an abuse minimized way? Will you contribute to world peace? Will you dance? Will you clash?

Will you selflessly help others on the way? Will you do it with friends? Will you find new friends? Will you teach and be taught by friends?

Will you need no extra money? Will you need more money? Will you need less? Will you need more health? Will you need more freedom?

Will you smile? Will you cry? Will you find lasting happiness?

There is only one way of knowing, and that is trying.

Go learn, get the habit, start with the curricula presented in the book if you will, start learning this book itself if you will, criticize it please, burn it to intellectual ashes if you can, or get convinced by it if you find it reasonable, adapt CDL to your country’s situation, whatever, just do it, learn, explore, seek happiness.
